1.
 
Strategic
 
Vision
 
and
 
M ission
 
Alignment
1.1
 
Deﬁning
 
Success
 
for
 
Desjardins
1.1.1
 
Core
 
Pillars
 
of
 
Success
1.
 
Financial
 
Health
 
○
 
Maintain
 
Robust
 
Proﬁtability
:
■
 
Balance
 
cost
 
management
 
with
 
targeted
 
investments
 
in
 
member
 
services
 
and
 
innovation.
■
 
Reinvest
 
portions
 
of
 
earnings
 
into
 
community
 
initiatives—like
 
local
 
business
 
grants
 
or
 
educational
 
programs—to
 
reinforce
 
Desjardins’
 
cooperative
 
ethos.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Set
 
annual
 
proﬁtability
 
targets
 
that
 
simultaneously
 
account
 
for
 
reinvestment
 
thresholds.
 
If
 
proﬁtability
 
exceeds
 
forecasts,
 
increase
 
community
 
outreach
 
funding
 
proportionally.
○
 
Innovation
 
and
 
Sustainability
:
■
 
Incorporate
 
sustainable
 
practices
 
(e.g.,
 
green
 
infrastructure,
 
paperless
 
operations)
 
into
 
ﬁnancial
 
planning.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Allocate
 
a
 
set
 
percentage
 
of
 
the
 
annual
 
budget
 
for
 
“green
 
transition”
 
projects
 
(e.g.,
 
upgrading
 
to
 
energy-efficient
 
systems),
 
tracking
 
ROI
 
through
 
cost
 
savings
 
and
 
reduced
 
carbon
 
footprint.
2.
 
Member
 
Value
 
○
 
Competitive
 
Financial
 
Products
:
■
 
Provide
 
interest
 
rates,
 
loan
 
terms,
 
and
 
dividends
 
that
 
rival
 
or
 
surpass
 
market
 
offerings—while
 
focusing
 
on
 
member-centric
 
objectives
 
like
 
fair
 
pricing
 
and
 
inclusive
 
access.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Periodically
 
benchmark
 
your
 
product
 
suite
 
against
 
peer
 
institutions.
 
If
 
rates
 
become
 
uncompetitive,
 
restructure
 
fees
 
or
 
dividends
 
to
 
preserve
 
Desjardins’
 
position
 
as
 
a
 
top
 
cooperative
 
option.
○
 
Enhanced
 
Accessibility
:
■
 
Target
 
underserved
 
communities
 
by
 
simplifying
 
account
 
setup,
 
lowering
 
minimum
 
balance
 
requirements,
 
and
 
offering
 
bilingual
 
or
 
multicultural
 
member
 
support.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Launch
 
speciﬁc
 
outreach
 
campaigns—like
 
“Banking
 
for
 
All”
 
fairs—that
 
educate
 
prospective
 
members
 
on
 
how
 
Desjardins’
 
services
 
align
 
with
 
their
 
needs.
 
Track
 
new
 
account
 
openings
 
to
 
measure
 
impact.
3.
 
Community
 
Impact
 

○
 
Social
 
and
 
Economic
 
Improvements
:
■
 
Prioritize
 
funding
 
for
 
local
 
projects
 
that
 
boost
 
regional
 
development
 
(e.g.,
 
incubators
 
for
 
small
 
entrepreneurs,
 
scholarships
 
for
 
youth
 
education).
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Establish
 
a
 
community
 
advisory
 
board
 
that
 
meets
 
quarterly
 
to
 
identify
 
high-impact
 
local
 
projects
 
deserving
 
of
 
Desjardins’
 
support.
○
 
Leadership
 
in
 
Local
 
Initiatives
:
■
 
Facilitate
 
ﬁnancial
 
literacy
 
workshops,
 
entrepreneurship
 
mentorship
 
programs,
 
and
 
networking
 
events
 
to
 
strengthen
 
community
 
ties.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Encourage
 
employees
 
to
 
volunteer
 
for
 
these
 
programs,
 
offering
 
time-off
 
incentives.
 
Publish
 
outcomes
 
(jobs
 
created,
 
businesses
 
launched)
 
to
 
showcase
 
progress.
4.
 
Resilience
 
○
 
Adaptable
 
Organizational
 
Structures
:
■
 
Anticipate
 
market
 
shifts,
 
technology
 
advancements,
 
and
 
regulatory
 
changes
 
by
 
embedding
 
ﬂexibility
 
in
 
operations
 
and
 
governance.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Conduct
 
annual
 
scenario-planning
 
exercises,
 
testing
 
Desjardins’
 
response
 
to
 
events
 
like
 
economic
 
downturns
 
or
 
sudden
 
ﬁntech
 
disruptions.
 
Adjust
 
processes
 
based
 
on
 
identiﬁed
 
vulnerabilities.
○
 
Continuous
 
Skill
 
Development
:
■
 
Train
 
employees
 
in
 
emerging
 
trends
 
(e.g.,
 
digital
 
banking,
 
ESG
 
compliance),
 
ensuring
 
Desjardins
 
can
 
quickly
 
pivot
 
to
 
meet
 
evolving
 
member
 
demands.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Introduce
 
a
 
structured
 
“Resilience
 
Curriculum”
 
offering
 
online
 
modules
 
on
 
crisis
 
management
 
and
 
data
 
analytics.

1.1.2
 
Balancing
 
Cooperative
 
Values
 
and
 
Financial
 
Competitiveness
1.
 
Cooperative
 
Values
 
○
 
Transparency
 
and
 
Participation
:
■
 
Involve
 
members
 
in
 
major
 
decisions—like
 
product
 
launches
 
or
 
community
 
investment
 
directions—through
 
surveys,
 
town
 
halls,
 
or
 
digital
 
voting
 
platforms.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Schedule
 
quarterly
 
“M ember
 
Policy
 
Forums”
 
to
 
solicit
 
input
 
on
 
proposed
 
changes
 
(e.g.,
 
new
 
loan
 
terms),
 
ensuring
 
decisions
 
reﬂect
 
the
 
broader
 
membership’s
 
voice.
○
 
Solidarity
 
and
 
Collective
 
Prosperity
:
■
 
Uphold
 
Desjardins’
 
founding
 
principle
 
of
 
mutual
 
aid,
 
ensuring
 
all
 
strategic
 
plans
 
prioritize
 
community
 
well-being
 
over
 
short-term
 
proﬁts.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
For
 
every
 
new
 
initiative,
 
require
 
a
 
brief
 
“Cooperative
 
Impact
 
Assessment”
 
to
 
articulate
 
its
 
beneﬁts
 
to
 
members
 
and
 
communities
 
(e.g.,
 
job
 
creation,
 
ﬁnancial
 
inclusion).
2.
 
Financial
 
Competitiveness
 
○
 
Modern
 
Banking
 
Tools
:
■
 
Adopt
 
data
 
analytics,
 
AI-driven
 
loan
 
underwriting,
 
and
 
user-friendly
 
digital
 
channels
 
to
 
meet
 
member
 
expectations
 
efficiently.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Periodically
 
review
 
digital
 
adoption
 
rates.
 
If
 
usage
 
is
 
low,
 
launch
 
targeted
 
education
 
sessions
 
or
 
streamline
 
user
 
interfaces
 
to
 
boost
 
engagement.
○
 
Economies
 
of
 
Scale
:
■
 
Collaborate
 
with
 
regional
 
caisses
 
to
 
centralize
 
back-office
 
tasks
 
(e.g.,
 
risk
 
management,
 
IT
 
infrastructure)
 
while
 
allowing
 
each
 
caisse
 
autonomy
 
in
 
community
 
engagement.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Form
 
task
 
forces
 
to
 
identify
 
duplication
 
of
 
services
 
and
 
propose
 
shared
 
solutions
 
(e.g.,
 
a
 
centralized
 
call
 
center).
 
M easure
 
cost
 
savings
 
and
 
re-channel
 
them
 
into
 
member
 
beneﬁts.

1.1.3
 
Long-Term
 
Vision
 
for
 
Sustainable
 
Growth
1.
 
Sustainability
 
as
 
a
 
Guiding
 
Principle
 
○
 
Integrate
 
ESG
 
Factors
:
■
 
Incorporate
 
environmental,
 
social,
 
and
 
governance
 
considerations
 
into
 
product
 
design,
 
vendor
 
selection,
 
and
 
operational
 
decisions.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Develop
 
a
 
“Green
 
Scorecard”
 
for
 
products,
 
evaluating
 
carbon
 
footprint,
 
social
 
impact,
 
and
 
governance
 
metrics.
 
Use
 
this
 
scorecard
 
when
 
deciding
 
whether
 
to
 
launch,
 
continue,
 
or
 
discontinue
 
offerings.
○
 
Measurable
 
Sustainability
 
Targets
:
■
 
Set
 
clear
 
benchmarks
 
(e.g.,
 
30%
 
reduction
 
in
 
operational
 
carbon
 
footprint
 
within
 
ﬁve
 
years,
 
doubling
 
the
 
number
 
of
 
green
 
loans
 
each
 
year).
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Review
 
performance
 
against
 
these
 
targets
 
quarterly.
 
If
 
progress
 
lags,
 
reallocate
 
budgets
 
or
 
introduce
 
new
 
incentives
 
(like
 
better
 
loan
 
rates
 
for
 
eco-friendly
 
borrowers).
2.
 
Innovation-Driven
 
Growth
 
○
 
Emerging
 
Trends
 
in
 
Fintech
 
and
 
Regulation
:
■
 
Stay
 
ahead
 
of
 
regulatory
 
changes
 
(e.g.,
 
open
 
banking)
 
and
 
technological
 
developments
 
(e.g.,
 
AI-based
 
personalized
 
ﬁnance
 
advice).
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Establish
 
a
 
“Digital
 
Innovation
 
Council”
 
to
 
pilot
 
new
 
ideas—like
 
blockchain
 
for
 
secure
 
transactions—and
 
present
 
ﬁndings
 
to
 
the
 
Board
 
each
 
quarter.
○
 
Digital
 
Transformation
 
for
 
Accessibility
:
■
 
W hile
 
adopting
 
advanced
 
solutions,
 
ensure
 
members
 
lacking
 
digital
 
literacy
 
or
 
high-speed
 
internet
 
can
 
access
 
traditional
 
services.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
M aintain
 
a
 
minimum
 
branch
 
footprint
 
and
 
phone-based
 
services
 
for
 
remote
 
or
 
less
 
tech-savvy
 
members,
 
tracking
 
usage
 
to
 
balance
 
digital
 
and
 
offline
 
channels
 
effectively.
3.
 
Growth
 
Metrics
 
○
 
Deﬁning
 
Success
 
Indicators
:
■
 
Member
 
Satisfaction
:
 
Gather
 
net
 
promoter
 
scores,
 
complaint
 
resolutions,
 
and
 
satisfaction
 
surveys.
■
 
Community
 
Reinvestment
:
 
Calculate
 
what
 
percentage
 
of
 
proﬁts
 
is
 
channeled
 
into
 
local
 
projects
 
or
 
discounted
 
loans.
■
 
Shared
 
Returns
:
 
M onitor
 
growth
 
in
 
member
 
equity
 
(e.g.,
 
total
 
dividends,
 
patronage
 
refunds)
 
year-over-year.
■
 
Sustainable
 
Product
 
Expansion
:
 
Track
 
the
 
share
 
of
 
green
 
or
 
socially
 
beneﬁcial
 
products
 
in
 
the
 
total
 
portfolio.

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Present
 
these
 
metrics
 
in
 
a
 
“Cooperative
 
Scoreboard”
 
at
 
every
 
Board
 
meeting,
 
highlighting
 
areas
 
that
 
need
 
improvement
 
or
 
showcasing
 
successes
 
like
 
increased
 
member
 
equity
 
or
 
higher
 
adoption
 
of
 
green
 
products.
By
 
deﬁning
 
success
 
around
 
ﬁnancial
 
health,
 
member-centric
 
services,
 
tangible
 
community
 
impact,
 
and
 
resilience,
 
Desjardins
 
ensures
 
its
 
strategic
 
vision
 
stays
 
ﬁrmly
 
anchored
 
in
 
cooperative
 
principles.
 
Achieving
 
this
 
balance
 
between
 
cooperative
 
values
 
and
 
ﬁnancial
 
competitiveness
 
leads
 
to
 
sustainable,
 
mission-driven
 
growth—solidifying
 
Desjardins’
 
legacy
 
as
 
a
 
trusted,
 
community-focused
 
ﬁnancial
 
institution.

1.2
 
M ission
 
Integration
 
Across
 
Leadership
1.2.1
 
Embedding
 
Cooperative
 
Principles
 
into
 
Strategic
 
Decisions
●
 
Mission-Centered
 
Decision
 
Framework
 
○
 
Require
 
that
 
every
 
signiﬁcant
 
strategic
 
or
 
tactical
 
proposal
 
be
 
evaluated
 
against
 
cooperative
 
principles
 
before
 
approval.
■
 
For
 
instance,
 
when
 
considering
 
a
 
new
 
product
 
launch,
 
assess
 
whether
 
it
 
directly
 
serves
 
member
 
needs
 
or
 
community
 
welfare
 
alongside
 
proﬁtability
 
targets.
○
 
Encourage
 
scenario
 
planning
 
that
 
weighs
 
short-term
 
ﬁnancial
 
gains
 
against
 
potential
 
impacts
 
on
 
members
 
and
 
communities.
■
 
If
 
a
 
cost-cutting
 
measure
 
could
 
erode
 
service
 
quality,
 
develop
 
alternatives
 
that
 
retain
 
member
 
satisfaction.
●
 
Leadership
 
Alignment
 
○
 
Establish
 
overarching
 
strategic
 
objectives
 
that
 
each
 
Board
 
member,
 
executive,
 
and
 
manager
 
explicitly
 
commits
 
to
 
supporting.
■
 
Link
 
these
 
objectives
 
to
 
measurable
 
metrics—e.g.,
 
percentage
 
growth
 
in
 
member
 
equity
 
or
 
community
 
investments—so
 
that
 
alignment
 
is
 
both
 
qualitative
 
and
 
quantitative.
○
 
Foster
 
frequent
 
dialogue
 
among
 
leadership
 
tiers
 
to
 
ensure
 
consistency
 
in
 
implementing
 
cooperative-driven
 
goals.
■
 
Host
 
quarterly
 
cross-functional
 
leadership
 
meetings
 
to
 
review
 
progress
 
on
 
shared
 
priorities
 
(e.g.,
 
improved
 
local
 
reinvestment
 
strategies,
 
increased
 
member
 
participation
 
in
 
governance).
●
 
Policy
 
Filters
 
for
 
Cooperative
 
Alignment
 
○
 
Develop
 
a
 
structured
 
checklist
 
or
 
“cooperative
 
lens”
 
to
 
evaluate
 
all
 
major
 
initiatives:
■
 
Member
 
Priority
 
Check
:
 
Does
 
the
 
initiative
 
enhance
 
member
 
well-being
 
or
 
address
 
a
 
speciﬁc
 
member
 
need?
■
 
Environmental
 
and
 
Social
 
Alignment
:
 
Does
 
the
 
initiative
 
support
 
Desjardins’
 
sustainability
 
commitments
 
or
 
create
 
measurable
 
positive
 
community
 
impact?
■
 
Transparency
 
and
 
Participation
:
 
Can
 
members
 
easily
 
understand
 
and
 
inﬂuence
 
this
 
decision
 
if
 
necessary?
○
 
Incorporate
 
these
 
ﬁlters
 
into
 
existing
 
approval
 
processes,
 
ensuring
 
every
 
proposed
 
action
 
aligns
 
with
 
Desjardins’
 
foundational
 
values.

1.2.2
 
M aintaining
 
Alignment
 
Between
 
M ember
 
Expectations
 
and
 
Institutional
 
Goals
●
 
Data-Driven
 
Understanding
 
of
 
Members
 
○
 
Use
 
advanced
 
analytics
 
to
 
parse
 
transaction
 
data,
 
engagement
 
frequency,
 
and
 
product
 
usage
 
patterns
 
to
 
identify
 
shifts
 
in
 
member
 
behavior.
■
 
For
 
example,
 
if
 
younger
 
members
 
show
 
high
 
digital
 
engagement,
 
prioritize
 
improving
 
mobile
 
banking
 
features
 
and
 
digital
 
advisory
 
services.
○
 
Segment
 
members
 
by
 
demographic
 
or
 
ﬁnancial
 
needs
 
(e.g.,
 
entrepreneurs,
 
ﬁrst-time
 
mortgage
 
seekers)
 
to
 
deliver
 
highly
 
relevant
 
ﬁnancial
 
solutions.
●
 
Communication
 
and
 
Feedback
 
Mechanisms
 
○
 
Implement
 
ongoing
 
feedback
 
loops:
■
 
Real-Time
 
Channels
:
 
Online
 
surveys
 
and
 
app-based
 
feedback
 
prompts
 
to
 
capture
 
immediate
 
reactions
 
to
 
new
 
products
 
or
 
policy
 
changes.
■
 
Focus
 
Groups
:
 
Quarterly
 
sessions
 
with
 
diverse
 
member
 
segments
 
to
 
test
 
ideas
 
before
 
large-scale
 
rollouts.
○
 
Organize
 
annual
 
strategic
 
reviews
 
where
 
member
 
representatives
 
can
 
voice
 
priorities:
■
 
Present
 
the
 
year’s
 
achievements
 
and
 
shortfalls.
■
 
Collect
 
suggestions
 
that
 
directly
 
feed
 
into
 
the
 
next
 
strategic
 
planning
 
cycle.
●
 
Goal
 
Synchronization
 
○
 
Establish
 
a
 
set
 
of
 
KPIs
 
that
 
link
 
member
 
outcomes
 
to
 
institutional
 
objectives:
■
 
Member
 
Satisfaction
 
Index
:
 
Track
 
factors
 
like
 
service
 
quality,
 
responsiveness,
 
and
 
perceived
 
fairness
 
of
 
fees
 
or

Ratio
:

○

biannual

comparing

Frameworks
●

Hierarchies
 
○

:

and

■
 
Actionable
 
Tip:

for

that

affect

ﬁnancial

○

:

to

ﬁnance,

and

(e.g.,

○

to

for

that

(e.g.,

productivity
 
enhancements)
 
back
 
to
 
cooperative
 
outcomes
 
(e.g.,
 
member
 
satisfaction).
●

Protocols
 
○
 
Deﬁne
 
explicit
 
thresholds
 
that
 
trigger

for

review.
■
 
Example:

or

○
 
M aintain
 
a
 
clear
 
communication
 
chain
 
so
 
that
 
urgent
 
issues
 
are
 
escalated
 
promptly
 
without
 
unnecessary
 
bureaucratic
 
delays.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip:
 
Use

and

to

to

right
 
governance
 
body.

Meeting
 
Efficiency
●
 
Structured
 
Agendas
 
○
 
Pre-circulate
 
agendas
 
emphasizing
 
critical
 
decisions.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip:
 
Require
 
each

item
 
to
 
state
 
a
 
clear
 
objective
 
(e.g.,
 
“Decision
 
Needed,”
 
“Discussion,”
 
“Informational
 
Update”)
 
to

focused
 
use
 
of
 
time.
○
 
Limit
 
meeting
 
frequency
 
and
 
duration
 
by
 
aligning
 
topics
 
with
 
each
 
governance
 
body’s
 
mandate.
■
 
Example:
 
Board
 
meetings
 
for
 
high-level
 
strategy
 
once
 
a
 
month;
 
executive
 
committees
 
convene
 
weekly
 
or

as
 
necessary.
●

○

strict

limits
 
for
 
discussions
 
and
 
decisions:
■
 
Example:
 
10
 
minutes
 
for
 
presentations,
 
followed
 
by
 
10
 
minutes
 
of

○
 
Assign
 
a
 
timekeeper
 
to
 
enforce
 
adherence.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip:
 
Conclude
 
each
 
agenda
 
item
 
with
 
a
 
clear
 
outcome
 
(decision
 
made,

or
 
requires
 
further
 
analysis).
●

○

(e.g.,

for

decisions.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip:
 
Establish

for

load.
○
 
Provide

and

electronically
 
so

can

or

at

convenience.
Crisis

Protocols

Frameworks
 
○

speciﬁc
 
action
 
plans
 
for
 
possible
 
crises
 
such
 
as

shortfalls,

breaches,
 
or

events.

Actionable
 
Tip:
 
Store
 
crisis
 
playbooks
 
on

secure

platform
 
accessible
 
to
 
leadership
 
during

○
 
Deﬁne
 
clear

(ﬁnancial
 
ratios,

thresholds,
 
or

that

(L CR)
 
dips

convene

M anagement

of
 
Roles
 
○

or

forces
 
to

crises
 
based

(e.g.,

Team,

Force).
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip:
 
M aintain
 
an
 
up-to-date

list
 
and
 
a

chart
 
so
 
that
 
each

knows
 
their
 
responsibilities
 
without

○
 
Authorize
 
expedited
 
decision-making

for
 
these
 
committees
 
when

is
 
officially

■
 
Example:
 
The
 
Finance
 
Committee
 
can
 
unilaterally
 
approve
 
emergency
 
funding
 
lines
 
to
 
stabilize

By

and

robust

protocols,
 
Desjardins
 
enhances

to

and

changes
 
while

the
 
cooperative
 
principles
 
at
 
the

or

move.

Channels

M anagement)

:

Role
 
Clarity
●

○

among

:
 
M aintain

○

high-level

:
 
For

M anagement

○

ﬁndings

:

wherein
 
committees
 
conﬁrm
 
action
 
plan
 
outcomes
 
after

team’s

2.2.1
 
Key
 
Performance
 
Indicators
 
(KPIs)

Strategic

KPIs
1.
 
Alignment
 
of
 
Strategic
 
Objectives
 
with
 
Cooperative
 
Values
 
○
 
Measurement
:
 
Periodic
 
member
 
surveys
 
and
 
focus
 
groups,
 
assessing
 
member
 
perception
 
of
 
whether
 
Desjardins’
 
initiatives
 
uphold
 
cooperative
 
principles.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Compare
 
survey
 
results
 
across
 
different
 
regions
 
or
 
member
 
segments
 
to
 
identify
 
alignment
 
gaps.
 
If
 
certain
 
branches
 
or
 
products
 
receive
 
lower
 
“values
 
alignment”
 
scores,
 
investigate
 
root
 
causes
 
and
 
adjust
 
strategies
 
accordingly.
2.
 
Execution

Initiatives
 
○

:

of

to

planned
 
within

ﬁscal
 
year,
 
along
 
with

and

○

Tip
:

Achieved

If

Risk
 
Management
 
KPIs
1.
 
Risk-Adjusted
 
Return
 
on
 
Assets
 
(RAROA)
 
○
 
Measurement
:
 
Financial
 
returns
 
weighted
 
against
 
overall
 
risk
 
exposure,
 
indicating
 
whether
 
governance
 
bodies
 
are
 
balancing
 
proﬁtability
 
and
 
risk
 
appropriately.

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Align
 
incentive
 
structures
 
so
 
that
 
executives
 
are
 
rewarded
 
not
 
just
 
for
 
returns
 
but
 
also
 
for
 
prudent
 
risk
 
management.
2.
 
Number
 
and
 
Severity
 
of
 
Identiﬁed
 
and
 
Mitigated
 
Risks
 
○
 
Measurement
:
 
Track
 
risk
 
events
 
reported
 
during
 
each
 
quarter
 
(e.g.,
 
cybersecurity
 
threats,
 
credit
 
portfolio
 
concerns)
 
and
 
classify
 
them
 
by
 
severity.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Apply
 
root
 
cause
 
analysis
 
for
 
the
 
top
 
three
 
most
 
severe
 
risks
 
each
 
quarter.
 
Present
 
mitigation
 
plans
 
to
 
the
 
Risk
 
M anagement
 
Committee
 
for
 
expedited
 
oversight.
3.
 
Compliance
 
with
 
Regulatory
 
Audit
 
Standards
 
○
 
Measurement
:
 
Frequency
 
of
 
non-conformities
 
noted
 
in
 
regulatory
 
audits
 
(targeting
 
zero
 
critical
 
ﬁndings).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Automate
 
tracking
 
of
 
internal
 
policy
 
adherence
 
(e.g.,
 
anti-money
 
laundering
 
protocols)
 
and
 
generate
 
real-time
 
alerts
 
when
 
deviations
 
occur,
 
allowing
 
committees
 
to
 
address
 
issues
 
before
 
they
 
escalate.
Compliance
 
KPIs
1.
 
Percentage
 
of
 
Adherence
 
to
 
Internal
 
Policies
 
and
 
External
 
Regulations
 
○
 
Measurement
:
 
M onthly
 
or
 
quarterly
 
compliance
 
reports
 
indicating
 
areas
 
fully
 
compliant
 
vs.
 
those
 
requiring
 
remedial
 
actions.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Introduce
 
a
 
“compliance
 
scorecard”
 
across
 
all
 
departments.
 
Departments
 
consistently
 
scoring
 
below
 
target
 
should
 
submit
 
improvement
 
plans
 
to
 
the
 
Audit
 
and
 
Compliance
 
Committee.
2.
 
Timeliness
 
of
 
Reporting
 
to
 
Regulatory
 
Bodies
 
and
 
Stakeholders
 
○
 
Measurement
:
 
Average
 
time
 
from
 
reporting
 
requirement
 
issuance
 
to
 
official
 
submission;
 
use
 
a
 
compliance
 
calendar
 
to
 
avoid
 
late
 
ﬁlings.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Assign
 
a
 
dedicated
 
compliance
 
coordinator
 
to
 
each
 
major
 
regulatory
 
or
 
stakeholder
 
report.
 
Track
 
whether
 
deadlines
 
are
 
met
 
or
 
if
 
extensions
 
are
 
needed.
3.
 
Effectiveness
 
of
 
Whistleblower
 
Programs
 
○
 
Measurement
:
 
Number
 
of
 
whistleblower
 
reports
 
ﬁled
 
vs.
 
resolved
 
within
 
a
 
speciﬁc
 
timeframe
 
(e.g.,
 
30
 
or
 
60
 
days).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Conduct
 
anonymous
 
follow-up
 
surveys
 
of
 
whistleblowers
 
to
 
gauge
 
their
 
satisfaction
 
with
 
the
 
resolution
 
process.
 
High
 
satisfaction
 
rates
 
often
 
correlate
 
with
 
a
 
strong
 
ethical
 
culture.

Board
 
and
 
Committee
 
Effectiveness
1.
 
Attendance
 
Rates
 
and
 
Participation
 
Levels
 
○
 
Measurement
:
 
Track
 
absenteeism,
 
tardiness,
 
and
 
level
 
of
 
engagement
 
(e.g.,
 
questions
 
raised,
 
voting
 
participation).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Set
 
a
 
target
 
attendance
 
rate
 
(e.g.,
 
90%
 
minimum
 
for
 
Board
 
meetings).
 
If
 
members
 
consistently
 
underperform,
 
explore
 
either
 
schedule
 
adjustments
 
or
 
reevaluation
 
of
 
their
 
roles.
2.
 
Timeliness
 
of
 
Decision-Making
 
on
 
Critical
 
Issues
 
○
 
Measurement
:
 
Time
 
taken
 
to
 
reach
 
a
 
resolution
 
on
 
priority
 
matters
 
(e.g.,
 
crisis
 
funding
 
approvals,
 
major
 
acquisitions).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Enforce
 
deﬁned
 
decision-making
 
deadlines.
 
If
 
repeated
 
delays
 
occur,
 
revise
 
governance
 
protocols
 
(e.g.,
 
empower
 
committees
 
with
 
provisional
 
authority
 
under
 
speciﬁc
 
thresholds).

Member
 
Satisfaction
 
with
 
Governance
 
Processes
 
○

:

governance
 
reviews
 
involving
 
member

or

to

whether

and

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Publish
 
a
 
summary
 
of
 
governance
 
improvements
 
implemented
 
based
 
on
 
member
 
feedback,
 
reinforcing
 
trust
 
and
 
demonstrating
 
accountability.
By
 
monitoring
 
and
 
continuously

these
 
KPIs,
 
Desjardins’

and

teams
 
can
 
maintain
 
high

ﬁnancially

and

Regular

of

metrics—coupled

plans—ensures
 
that
 
all

are
 
proactively
 
adapting
 
to
 
internal

and

challenges,
 
reinforcing
 
Desjardins’
 
position
 
as

2.2.2
 
Periodic
 
Governance
 
Reviews
Periodic
 
governance
 
reviews
 
ensure
 
Desjardins’
 
governance
 
structure
 
remains
 
effective,
 
transparent,
 
and
 
closely
 
aligned
 
with
 
both
 
cooperative
 
values
 
and
 
regulatory
 
expectations.
 
By
 
conducting
 
these
 
evaluations
 
regularly—and
 
following
 
up
 
with
 
targeted
 
improvements—the
 
organization
 
fortiﬁes
 
its
 
capacity
 
to
 
make
 
informed
 
decisions
 
that
 
serve
 
members,
 
communities,
 
and
 
long-term
 
sustainability
 
goals.
Frequency
 
and
 
Scope
●
 
Annual
 
Comprehensive
 
Reviews
 
○
 
Purpose
:
 
Evaluate
 
the
 
efficiency
 
of
 
decision-making
 
processes,
 
as
 
well
 
as
 
the
 
overall
 
performance
 
of
 
governance
 
bodies
 
(the
 
Board,
 
executives,
 
and
 
committees).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Compile
 
a
 
“Governance
 
Scorecard”
 
each
 
year
 
that
 
tracks
 
KPIs
 
such
 
as
 
Board
 
engagement,
 
alignment
 
with
 
cooperative
 
principles,
 
and
 
compliance
 
metrics.
 
Present
 
this
 
scorecard
 
at
 
a
 
dedicated
 
review
 
meeting.
●
 
External
 
Audits
 
Every
 
Three
 
Years
 
○
 
Unbiased
 
Evaluation
:
 
Engaging
 
third-party
 
auditors
 
or
 
consultants
 
provides
 
an
 
independent
 
perspective
 
on
 
governance
 
efficacy.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Include
 
interviews
 
with
 
a
 
sampling
 
of
 
members,
 
community
 
partners,
 
and
 
other
 
stakeholders
 
in
 
the
 
audit
 
process.
 
This
 
helps
 
verify
 
that
 
strategic
 
and
 
operational
 
decisions
 
genuinely
 
reﬂect
 
Desjardins’
 
cooperative
 
mission.
Review
 
Methodology
●
 
Balanced
 
Scorecard
 
Approach
 
○
 
Holistic
 
Analysis
:
 
Go
 
beyond
 
ﬁnancial
 
performance
 
to
 
assess
 
operational
 
effectiveness
 
and
 
adherence
 
to
 
cooperative
 
ideals
 
(e.g.,
 
member
 
engagement,
 
sustainability
 
efforts).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Incorporate
 
ESG
 
(E nvironmental,
 
Social,
 
and
 
Governance)
 
metrics
 
within
 
the
 
balanced
 
scorecard
 
to
 
gauge
 
progress
 
on
 
environmental
 
impact,
 
social
 
outreach,
 
and
 
ethical
 
governance
 
practices.
●
 
Anonymous
 
Surveys
 
○
 
Qualitative
 
Feedback
:
 
Distribute
 
conﬁdential
 
questionnaires
 
to
 
Board
 
members,
 
executives,
 
and
 
committee
 
participants,
 
capturing
 
honest
 
perspectives
 
on
 
governance
 
strengths
 
and
 
weaknesses.

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Summarize
 
survey
 
ﬁndings
 
in
 
a
 
report
 
that
 
highlights
 
recurring
 
issues
 
or
 
themes,
 
and
 
schedule
 
a

workshop
 
to
 
brainstorm
 
solutions
 
and
 
share
 
best
 
practices.
●
 
Benchmark
 
Comparisons
 
○
 
Industry
 
Standards
 
and
 
Internal
 
Targets
:
 
Compare
 
governance
 
performance
 
metrics
 
against
 
sector-wide
 
best
 
practices,
 
credit

networks,
 
or

as
 
well
 
as
 
Desjardins’
 
own
 
historical

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Track
 
improvements
 
(or

in
 
key
 
areas—like
 
meeting
 
efficiency
 
or
 
risk
 
management—and
 
attribute

to
 
speciﬁc

in

Adjustments
 
and
 
Improvements
●
 
Formal
 
Process
 
for
 
Acting
 
on
 
Review
 
Findings
 
○
 
Continuous
 
Improvement
:
 
Establish
 
a

step-by-step
 
protocol
 
for
 
incorporating
 
review
 
outcomes
 
into
 
governance
 
structures.
 
This
 
may
 
include
 
immediate
 
corrective
 
actions
 
or
 
strategic
 
recommendations
 
for
 
the
 
upcoming
 
planning
 
cycle.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Present
 
signiﬁcant
 
ﬁndings
 
at
 
a
 
Board
 
meeting
 
dedicated
 
to
 
governance
 
reﬁnement.
 
Require
 
each
 
major
 
recommendation
 
to

a
 
named
 
sponsor
 
(e.g.,
 
a
 
Board
 
member
 
or
 
executive)
 
responsible
 
for
 
overseeing
 
implementation.
●
 
Revising
 
Committee
 
Charters
 
and
 
Mandates
 
○
 
Targeted
 
Realignment
:
 
If
 
a
 
review
 
indicates
 
that
 
a
 
committee’s
 
scope
 
overlaps
 
with
 
another
 
or
 
is
 
no
 
longer
 
relevant,
 
update
 
its
 
charter
 
or
 
consider
 
merging
 
committees.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Introduce
 
pilot
 
phases
 
for
 
revised
 
committee
 
structures,
 
so
 
the
 
Board
 
can
 
assess
 
effectiveness
 
before
 
ﬁnalizing
 
long-term
 
changes.
●
 
Adjusting
 
Decision-Making
 
Protocols
 
○
 
Eliminating
 
Inefficiencies
:
 
Based
 
on
 
review
 
insights,
 
streamline
 
or
 
clarify
 
escalation
 
procedures,
 
reporting
 
lines,
 
and
 
frequency
 
of
 
meetings.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
If
 
decisions
 
frequently
 
stall
 
at

particular
 
approval
 
level,
 
empower
 
relevant
 
committees
 
or
 
executives
 
with

ensuring

in
 
place.
●
 
Governance
 
Training
 
and
 
Development
 
○
 
Underperforming
 
Leaders
 
or
 
Teams
:
 
Implement
 
targeted
 
programs—from

bolster
 
governance
 
competencies.

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Use

of

within
 
Desjardins
 
or
 
from

ﬁndings—Desjardins

This

allows

to

safeguard
 
cooperative

and
 
deliver

ﬁnancial

2.2.3
 
Tools
 
for
 
Governance
 
Monitoring
A
 
structured
 
approach
 
to
 
governance
 
monitoring
 
is
 
essential
 
for
 
maintaining
 
transparency,
 
accountability,
 
and
 
alignment
 
with
 
Desjardins’
 
cooperative
 
principles.
 
Two
 
critical
 
tools
 
facilitate
 
effective
 
oversight:
 
integrated
 
governance
 
dashboards
 
and
 
self-assessment
 
templates.
 
By
 
using
 
these
 
resources
 
consistently,
 
Board
 
members
 
and
 
executives
 
can
 
spot
 
emerging
 
issues
 
quickly,
 
ensure
 
compliance,
 
and
 
strengthen
 
strategic
 
execution.
Integrated
 
Governance
 
Dashboard
●
 
Real-Time
 
KPI
 
Tracking
 
○
 
Purpose
:
 
Provide
 
a
 
single,
 
centralized
 
view
 
of
 
key
 
governance
 
metrics—such
 
as
 
risk
 
exposure,
 
compliance
 
status,
 
and
 
progress
 
on
 
strategic
 
goals.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Update
 
dashboards
 
automatically
 
using
 
data
 
feeds
 
from
 
multiple
 
internal
 
systems
 
(e.g.,
 
ﬁnance,
 
risk
 
management,
 
operations)
 
to
 
minimize
 
manual
 
data
 
entry
 
and
 
reduce
 
errors.
○
 
Outcome
:
 
Enables
 
Board
 
members
 
and
 
executives
 
to
 
make
 
prompt,
 
informed
 
decisions
 
based
 
on
 
the
 
most
 
recent
 
information,
 
preventing
 
issues
 
from
 
escalating
 
unnoticed.
●
 
Visual
 
Summaries
 
of
 
Institutional
 
Performance
 
○
 
Purpose
:
 
Offer
 
concise,

representations
 
(e.g.,
 
charts,
 
heat
 
maps)
 
that
 
highlight
 
trends,
 
outliers,
 
or
 
areas
 
of
 
concern
 
at
 
a
 
glance.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Implement
 
color-coded
 
status
 
indicators
 
(green,
 
yellow,
 
red)
 
for
 
quick
 
priority
 
assessment—ensuring
 
that
 
busy
 
leaders
 
immediately
 
recognize
 
which
 
areas
 
need
 
urgent
 
attention.
○
 
Outcome
:
 
Facilitates
 
efficient
 
Board
 
and
 
committee
 
meetings
 
by
 
shortening
 
the
 
time
 
spent
 
interpreting
 
data
 
and
 
allowing
 
deeper
 
focus
 
on
 
strategic
 
or
 
high-risk
 
items.

Templates

3.1
 
Advanced
 
Financial
 
Strategies
3.1.1
 
Capital
 
Allocation
 
for
 
M aximum
 
M ember
 
Value
 
and
 
Sustainability
Proper
 
capital
 
allocation
 
is
 
critical
 
for
 
balancing
 
proﬁtability,
 
community
 
beneﬁts,
 
and

responsibility.
 
Bank

should
 
ensure
 
that
 
every

or

not
 
only
 
delivers
 
an
 
acceptable
 
ﬁnancial

but
 
also
 
aligns
 
with
 
Desjardins’

mission.
Capital
 
Allocation
 
Principles
●
 
Cooperative
 
and
 
Member
 
Beneﬁt
 
Alignment
 
○
 
Prioritize
 
projects
 
and
 
ﬁnancial
 
products
 
that
 
directly
 
improve
 
member
 
well-being,
 
foster
 
economic
 
inclusion,
 
or
 
strengthen
 
local
 
communities.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Require
 
every
 
funding
 
proposal
 
to
 
include
 
a
 
“member
 
impact
 
statement,”
 
detailing
 
how
 
it
 
enhances
 
member
 
equity,
 
community
 
development,
 
or
 
overall
 
ﬁnancial
 
resilience.
●
 
Short-Term
 
vs.
 
Long-Term
 
Balance
 
○
 
Complement
 
near-term
 
revenue
 
generation
 
with
 
long-term
 
investments
 
in
 
community
 
growth,
 
environmental
 
sustainability,
 
and
 
innovation.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Designate
 
a
 
portion
 
of
 
the
 
budget
 
(e.g.,
 
10–15%)
 
for
 
initiatives
 
with
 
longer
 
payback
 
periods
 
but
 
high
 
social
 
and
 
environmental
 
impact
 
(such
 
as
 
green
 
infrastructure
 
or
 
affordable
 
housing).

with
 
ﬁntech

:

via

that

ﬁnancial

and

with

3.1.2
 
Liquidity
 
Management
Liquidity
 
management
 
is
 
a
 
cornerstone
 
of
 
Desjardins’
 
ﬁnancial
 
stability
 
and
 
member
 
trust.
 
Bank
 
directors
 
must
 
ensure
 
that
 
adequate
 
cash
 
or
 
easily
 
convertible
 
assets
 
are
 
available
 
at
 
all
 
times
 
to
 
meet
 
short-term
 
obligations,
 
safeguard
 
against
 
unexpected
 
withdrawals,
 
and
 
seize
 
strategic
 
opportunities.
 
By
 
balancing
 
internal
 
and
 
external
 
funding
 
sources
 
while
 
mitigating
 
risks
 
through
 
diversiﬁed
 
approaches,
 
Desjardins
 
can
 
maintain
 
a
 
resilient
 
liquidity
 
position
 
that
 
supports
 
its
 
cooperative
 
mission.
Liquidity
 
Framework
●
 
Maintaining
 
Sufficient
 
Liquid
 
Assets
 
○
 
Goal
:
 
Keep
 
a
 
robust
 
“liquidity
 
buffer”
 
to
 
handle
 
day-to-day
 
needs
 
and
 
sudden
 
cash
 
outﬂows
 
from
 
member
 
withdrawals
 
or
 
ﬁnancial
 
shocks.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Set
 
internal
 
liquidity
 
targets
 
(e.g.,
 
a
 
speciﬁc
 
ratio
 
of
 
liquid
 
assets
 
to
 
total
 
assets)
 
that
 
exceed
 
regulatory
 
requirements.
 
Regularly
 
review
 
these
 
targets
 
in
 
light
 
of
 
economic
 
conditions
 
and
 
membership
 
growth.

●
 
Real-Time
 
Monitoring
 
and
 
Forecasting
 
○
 
Approach
:
 
Deploy
 
systems
 
that
 
track
 
intra-day
 
cash
 
ﬂows
 
and
 
project
 
future
 
liquidity
 
demands
 
based
 
on
 
historical
 
patterns,
 
seasonal
 
trends,
 
and

indicators.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Use

forecasting
 
(e.g.,

scenarios)
 
to

could

at

Present

at

and

to
 
support

decisions.

Sources

in

Sources

:

■

:
 
M onitor

:

and

:

from

portfolios.

in

:

Risk
 
Mitigation
Proactive
 
measures
 
help
 
ensure
 
that
 
Desjardins’

remains
 
robust
 
under

and

conditions.
●

Testing
 
○
 
Objective
:
 
Identify
 
potential
 
vulnerabilities
 
by

like

outﬂows,

or

:

(e.g.,
 
an

downturn
 
vs.

Present
 
ﬁndings
 
to

Risk
 
M anagement
 
Committee

●

of

Sources
 
○
 
Goal
:
 
Reduce

on

Tip
:
 
M aintain

to

Key
 
Liquidity
 
Metrics

of

and
 
promotes
 
transparent
 
governance.
●
 
Liquidity
 
Coverage
 
Ratio
 
(LCR)
 
○
 
Purpose
:
 
M easures
 
short-term
 
liquidity
 
strength,
 
ensuring
 
the
 
institution
 
can
 
meet
 
30
 
days
 
of
 
expected
 
net
 
outﬂows
 
under
 
stressed
 
conditions.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Report
 
LCR
 
values
 
monthly.
 
If
 
levels
 
approach
 
regulatory
 
thresholds,
 
activate
 
contingency
 
plans
 
(e.g.,
 
draw
 
on

lines
 
or
 
issue
 
short-term
 
debt).
●
 
Net
 
Stable
 
Funding
 
Ratio
 
(NSFR)
 
○
 
Purpose
:
 
Gauges
 
the
 
stability
 
of
 
long-term
 
funding,
 
aligning
 
asset
 
maturities
 
with
 
liabilities.

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Align
 
product
 
offerings
 
(e.g.,
 
longer-term
 
ﬁxed
 
deposits)
 
with
 
asset
 
durations
 
to
 
maintain
 
or
 
improve
 
NSFR.
 
If
 
the
 
ratio
 
declines,
 
reconsider
 
investment
 
strategies
 
or
 
adjust
 
the
 
balance
 
of
 
short-
 
vs.
 
long-term
 
liabilities.
By
 
systematically
 
monitoring
 
liquidity,
 
diversifying
 
funding
 
sources,
 
and
 
conducting
 
regular
 
stress
 
tests,
 
Desjardins
 
can
 
protect
 
its
 
capacity
 
to
 
serve
 
members—even
 
during
 
economic
 
shocks.
 
Strong
 
liquidity
 
management
 
upholds
 
member
 
conﬁdence,
 
fosters
 
sustainable
 
growth,
 
and
 
reinforces
 
the
 
cooperative
 
model’s
 
emphasis
 
on
 
ﬁnancial
 
security
 
and
 
collective
 
well-being.

3.1.3

Risk
 
Management
Effective

management
 
balances
 
Desjardins’

mission—offering
 
equitable
 
and

lending—with
 
the

to

ﬁnancial

Bank

to

Credit
 
Allocation
 
Framework
●
 
Clear
 
Policies
 
for
 
Loan
 
Approvals
 
○
 
Goal
:
 
Establish
 
transparent
 
criteria
 
for
 
evaluating
 
borrower
 
proﬁles,
 
including

repayment

and
 
alignment
 
with
 
cooperative
 
values.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Require
 
a

“credit
 
approval

in

process.
 
The

should
 
capture
 
both

data
 
(e.g.,

ratios,

scores)
 
and

(e.g.,

to
 
sustainable
 
practices,
 
community
 
impact).
●
 
Sector
 
Prioritization
 
○
 
Strategy
:
 
Focus
 
on
 
sectors
 
offering

and

beneﬁts—such
 
as

or

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:

against

If

underperform
 
(e.g.,

in

loans),
 
conduct
 
member
 
outreach
 
or
 
reassess
 
product
 
terms
 
to
 
boost
 
participation.
Credit
 
Risk
 
Controls
●

Credit
 
Scoring
 
○
 
Purpose
:
 
Improve
 
accuracy
 
in

by

(e.g.,

alongside

(credit

ﬁnancial

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:

ﬁntech

M onitor

drift—a

where
 
predictive

declines
 
over
 
time—and
 
retrain
 
models
 
as
 
needed.
●

Portfolio
 
Monitoring
 

○
 
Objective
:
 
Detect
 
early
 
signs
 
of

or

allowing

(e.g.,

restructuring,
 
ﬁnancial

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Implement

triggers
 
in

that
 
ﬂag

For

occurs.
Loan
 
Diversiﬁcation
●

Portfolio
 
Across

and

○
 
Rationale
:
 
A

spreads

of

in
 
any

or

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Set
 
maximum

limits
 
per

(e.g.,

regularly
 
review
 
them.
 
If
 
one

approaches

slow

in

elsewhere.
●

High-Risk

While

○

:

to

or

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Implement

or

to
 
foster

Key
 
Credit
 
Metrics
●
 
Non-Performing
 
Loan
 
(NPL)
 
Ratio
 
○
 
Deﬁnition
:
 
The
 
percentage
 
of
 
loans
 
in
 
default
 
or
 
close
 
to
 
default.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Establish
 
NPL
 
thresholds
 
that
 
trigger
 
a
 
“watchlist”
 
process.
 
If
 
NPLs
 
exceed
 
a
 
set
 
percentage
 
(e.g.,
 
3%),
 
convene
 
an
 
urgent
 
credit
 
committee
 
review
 
to
 
identify
 
root
 
causes
 
(such
 
as
 
a
 
local
 
economic
 
slump
 
or
 
overly
 
lenient
 
lending
 
criteria).
●
 
Provision
 
Coverage
 
Ratio
 
○
 
Purpose
:
 
M easures
 
how
 
well
 
potential
 
loan
 
losses
 
are
 
covered
 
by
 
reserves.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Compare
 
current
 
provisions
 
against
 
historical
 
default
 
rates
 
and
 
economic
 
forecasts.
 
If
 
coverage
 
dips
 
below
 
target,
 
present
 
a

to
 
the
 
Board
 
outlining
 
how
 
you
 
will
 
increase
 
provisions
 
(e.g.,

process
 
or
 
reevaluating
 
sector
 
exposure).

By
 
employing
 
a
 
well-deﬁned

controls,
 
and

the

Desjardins
 
can
 
sustain
 
both
 
ﬁnancial

and

M onitoring
 
NPL
 
and
 
provision

ratios
 
helps
 
directors
 
rapidly

and
 
address
 
issues
 
before

escalate,
 
ensuring
 
that
 
Desjardins
 
remains
 
a
 
trusted,
 
resilient

for

and

3.1.4
 
Market
 
Risk
 
Management
M arket
 
risk
 
refers
 
to
 
the
 
potential
 
for
 
ﬁnancial
 
losses
 
arising
 
from
 
changes
 
in
 
market
 
conditions—such
 
as
 
interest
 
rates,
 
foreign
 
exchange
 
rates,
 
and
 
broader
 
economic
 
shifts—that
 
can
 
affect
 
Desjardins’
 
asset
 
and
 
liability
 
portfolios.
 
Bank
 
directors
 
must
 
proactively
 
identify,
 
measure,
 
and
 
mitigate
 
these
 
risks
 
to
 
ensure
 
the
 
institution’s
 
ﬁnancial
 
stability,
 
proﬁtability,
 
and
 
continued
 
service
 
to
 
members.
Risk
 
Sources
1.
 
Interest
 
Rate
 
Risk
 
○
 
Impact
 
of
 
Changing
 
Rates
■
 
Fluctuations
 
in
 
interest
 
rates
 
can
 
alter
 
the
 
value
 
of
 
loans,
 
deposits,
 
and
 
investment
 
securities.
 
A
 
sudden
 
rise
 
in
 
rates
 
may
 
compress
 
proﬁt
 
margins
 
if
 
deposit
 
rates
 
adjust
 
faster
 
than
 
loan
 
rates,
 
while
 
a
 
decline
 
can
 
affect
 
earnings
 
on
 
variable-rate
 
assets.
○
 
Mitigation
 
Through
 
Duration
 
Matching
■
 
Aim
 
to
 
align
 
the
 
maturities
 
(or
 
durations)
 
of
 
assets
 
and
 
liabilities.
 
This
 
helps
 
reduce
 
volatility
 
in
 
net
 
interest
 
income
 
when
 
rates
 
shift.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Implement
 
a
 
duration
 
gap
 
limit
 
(e.g.,
 
no
 
more
 
than
 
6
 
months’
 
mismatch
 
between
 
asset
 
and
 
liability
 
maturities).
 
Regularly
 
review
 
the
 
gap
 
in
 
executive
 
risk
 
committees
 
to
 
trigger
 
timely
 
hedging
 
or
 
portfolio
 
adjustments
 
if
 
it
 
exceeds
 
tolerances.
2.
 
Foreign
 
Exchange
 
Risk
 
○
 
Exposure
 
from
 
International
 
Operations
■
 
Desjardins
 
may
 
face
 
currency
 
ﬂuctuations
 
when
 
dealing
 
with
 
cross-border
 
transactions
 
or
 
investments
 
denominated
 
in
 
foreign
 
currencies.
○
 
Use
 
of
 
Hedging
 
Instruments
■
 
Employ
 
forwards,
 
swaps,
 
and
 
options
 
to
 
lock
 
in
 
exchange
 
rates
 
and
 
safeguard
 
earnings.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
If
 
Desjardins
 
operates
 
in
 
multiple
 
currencies,
 
set
 
a
 
maximum
 
unhedged
 
currency
 
exposure
 
limit
 
(e.g.,
 
a
 
percentage
 
of
 
capital).
 
Use
 
daily
 
dashboards
 
to
 
monitor
 
real-time
 
currency
 
positions,
 
ensuring
 
swift
 
corrective
 
actions
 
when
 
approaching
 
risk
 
thresholds.
Risk
 
Mitigation
 
Techniques

1.
 
Diversify
 
Investment
 
Portfolios
 
○
 
Spread
 
investments
 
across
 
various
 
asset
 
classes,
 
industries,
 
and
 
regions
 
to
 
reduce
 
exposure
 
to
 
single-market
 
downturns.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Review
 
portfolio
 
composition
 
quarterly.
 
If
 
exposure
 
in
 
one
 
sector
 
or
 
region
 
becomes
 
disproportionately
 
high
 
(e.g.,
 
exceeds
 
15–20%
 
of
 
the
 
total
 
portfolio),
 
reallocate
 
assets
 
or
 
use
 
derivative
 
instruments
 
to
 
mitigate
 
concentration
 
risk.
2.
 
Monitor
 
and
 
Adjust
 
Interest
 
Rate
 
Sensitivity
 
○
 
Regularly
 
measure
 
how
 
changes
 
in
 
interest
 
rates
 
affect
 
the
 
net
 
interest
 
margin
 
(N IM )
 
and
 
the
 
economic
 
value
 
of
 
equity
 
(E VE).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Conduct
 
interest
 
rate
 
stress
 
tests
 
(e.g.,
 
+/–100
 
or
 
200
 
basis
 
points)
 
and
 
report
 
results
 
to
 
the
 
Board.
 
If
 
models
 
predict
 
signiﬁcant
 
NIM
 
compression,
 
pursue
 
strategies
 
like
 
interest
 
rate
 
swaps
 
or
 
restructuring
 
liabilities
 
to
 
achieve
 
a
 
more
 
favorable
 
duration
 
mix.
Key
 
Market
 
Risk
 
Metrics
1.
 
Value
 
at
 
Risk
 
(VaR)
 
○
 
Purpose
:
 
Quantiﬁes
 
potential
 
losses
 
within
 
a
 
speciﬁed
 
conﬁdence
 
level
 
(e.g.,
 
99%)
 
and
 
time
 
horizon
 
(e.g.,
 
one
 
day).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Compare
 
VaR
 
estimates
 
against
 
risk
 
appetite
 
limits
 
set
 
by
 
the
 
Board.
 
If
 
VaR
 
approaches
 
or
 
exceeds
 
these
 
limits,
 
investigate
 
which
 
positions
 
are
 
driving
 
the
 
increase
 
and
 
consider
 
hedging,
 
reallocation,
 
or
 
more
 
conservative
 
underwriting.
2.
 
Interest
 
Rate
 
Sensitivity
 
Gap
 
○
 
Deﬁnition
:
 
The
 
mismatch
 
between
 
interest-bearing
 
assets
 
and
 
liabilities
 
over
 
speciﬁc
 
time
 
buckets
 
(e.g.,
 
1–3
 
months,
 
3–6
 
months).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Track
 
the
 
gap
 
monthly
 
and
 
set
 
triggers
 
(e.g.,
 
if
 
gap
 
exceeds
 
10%
 
of
 
total
 
assets
 
in
 
a
 
given
 
time
 
bucket).
 
If
 
the
 
threshold
 
is
 
breached,
 
take
 
corrective
 
measures
 
such
 
as
 
adjusting
 
loan
 
repricing
 
schedules,
 
offering
 
different-term
 
deposits,
 
or
 
using
 
swaps
 
to
 
stabilize
 
the
 
interest
 
rate
 
proﬁle.
By
 
continuously
 
monitoring
 
interest
 
rate
 
and
 
foreign
 
exchange
 
exposures,
 
diversifying
 
investment
 
portfolios,
 
and
 
leveraging
 
hedging
 
strategies,
 
Desjardins
 
can
 
control
 
market
 
risk
 
while
 
preserving
 
proﬁtability.
 
Directors
 
play
 
a
 
pivotal
 
role
 
by
 
approving
 
clear
 
risk
 
thresholds,
 
reviewing
 
stress
 
test
 

results,
 
and
 
ensuring
 
timely
 
corrective
 
actions,
 
all
 
of
 
which
 
uphold
 
Desjardins’
 
cooperative
 
commitment
 
to
 
ﬁnancial
 
security
 
and
 
member
 
well-being.

3.2
 
Enterprise
 
Risk
 
M anagement
 
(ERM )
3.2.1

Risk
 
Modeling
Predictive

modeling
 
equips
 
Desjardins
 
with

into

threats,

and

By

and

Desjardins
 
can

and

policies
 
accordingly,
 
and
 
safeguard
 
long-term

Scenario
 
Analysis
●

Multifaceted
 
Risk
 
Scenarios
 
1.
 
Approach
:

and

“what-if”

from

or

to

or

2.
 
Actionable

:
 
Update

annually
 
or
 
whenever
 
signiﬁcant
 
market
 
or
 
policy
 
shifts
 
occur
 
(e.g.,
 
interest
 
rate
 
changes,
 
new
 
regulations).
 
Present
 
scenario
 
outcomes
 
to
 
the
 
Board
 
and
 
key
 
committees
 
to
 
reﬁne
 
capital
 
allocation
 
and
 
business
 
continuity
 
plans.
●
 
Examples
 
of
 
Critical
 
Scenarios
 
1.
 
Economic
 
Downturn
:
 
Project
 
increased
 
defaults
 
on
 
loans
 
and
 
reduced
 
investment
 
returns
 
under
 
high
 
unemployment
 
or
 
inﬂation
 
conditions.
2.
 
Regulatory
 
Shifts
:
 
Assess
 
the
 
cost
 
implications
 
of
 
major
 
legal
 
or
 
compliance
 
changes
 
(e.g.,
 
stricter
 
data
 
protection
 
laws).
3.
 
Cybersecurity
 
Breaches
:
 
M odel
 
the
 
ﬁnancial
 
and
 
reputational
 
damage
 
from
 
IT
 
system
 
failures
 
or
 
data
 
compromises,
 
along
 
with
 
recovery
 
timelines.
Data-Driven
 
Risk
 
Models
●
 
AI
 
and

Learning
 
○
 
Value
:

pattern

and

using

(e.g.,

○

:

feeds—like

ﬂuctuations—into

○

:

(e.g.,

ﬁrms

into
 
risk
 
assessments.
Stress
 
Testing
●
 
Regular
 
Stress
 
Test
 
Cycles
 
1.
 
Objective
:
 
Gauge
 
Desjardins’
 
resilience
 
under
 
extreme
 
yet
 
plausible
 
conditions—such
 
as
 
sudden

2.
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Conduct
 
at

stress
 
tests
 
with

(mild,
 
moderate,
 
severe).
 
After

share
 
results
 
with
 
the
 
Risk
 
M anagement
 
Committee
 
for
 
swift

actions.
●
 
Focus
 
Areas
 
1.
 
Liquidity
 
Shocks
:
 
Evaluate
 
the

of
 
large-scale
 
withdrawals
 
or

on

:

from

in

Disruptions
:
 
Simulate
 
IT

or

shortages,

on

and

Output
 
Utilization
●

○
 
Strategy
:
 
Use
 
predictive
 
risk
 
model

to

○

:

●

○

:

:

By

3.2.2
 
Crisis
 
Management
 
Frameworks
A
 
robust
 
crisis
 
management
 
framework
 
safeguards
 
Desjardins
 
against
 
sudden
 
disruptions
 
that
 
can
 
compromise
 
member
 
trust,
 
ﬁnancial
 
stability,
 
and
 
cooperative
 
values.
 
Bank
 
directors
 
should
 
ensure
 
that
 
potential
 
crises
 
are
 
systematically
 
identiﬁed,
 
swiftly
 
contained,
 
and
 
thoroughly
 
analyzed
 
to
 
prevent
 
recurrence.
 
The
 
following
 
components
 
provide
 
a
 
structured
 
approach
 
to
 
crisis
 
preparedness
 
and
 
response.
Crisis
 
Identiﬁcation
●
 
Comprehensive
 
Risk
 
Register
 
○
 
Purpose
:
 
Catalog
 
all
 
potential
 
crisis
 
scenarios—spanning
 
ﬁnancial
 
(liquidity
 
shortages),
 
operational
 
(cyberattacks,
 
power
 
outages),
 
and
 
reputational
 
(p ublic
 
trust
 
erosion
 
due
 
to
 
governance
 
failures).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Regularly
 
update
 
the
 
register
 
with
 
new
 
risks
 
(e.g.,
 
emerging
 
technologies,
 
global
 
health
 
events).
 
Assign
 
a
 
risk
 
owner
 
for
 
each
 
crisis
 
type,
 
ensuring
 
accountability
 
for
 
ongoing
 
monitoring
 
and
 
mitigation.
●
 
Classiﬁcation
 
of
 
Potential
 
Crises
 
○
 
Categories
:
1.
 
Financial
 
Crises
:
 
Liquidity
 
or
 
capital
 
shortfalls,
 
large-scale
 
loan
 
defaults.
2.
 
Operational
 
Crises
:
 
Systems
 
downtime,
 
data
 
breaches,
 
severe
 
staffing
 
shortages.
3.
 
Reputational
 
Crises
:
 
Negative
 
media
 
coverage
 
or
 
public
 
backlash
 
affecting
 
member
 
conﬁdence.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
For
 
each
 
category,
 
deﬁne
 
early
 
warning
 
indicators
 
(e.g.,
 
deposit
 
outﬂow
 
rates,
 
IT
 
incident
 
reports,
 
sentiment
 
analysis
 
for
 
media
 
coverage).
 
Trigger
 
escalation
 
if
 
indicators
 
surpass
 
pre-determined
 
thresholds.
Response
 
Protocols
●
 
Predeﬁned
 
Escalation
 
Procedures
 
○
 
Immediate
 
Response
 
Teams
 
(IRTs)
■
 
Function
:
 
Rapidly
 
contain
 
crises
 
and
 
organize
 
initial
 
mitigation
 
steps
 
(e.g.,
 
isolating
 
affected
 
systems
 
in
 
a
 
cyberattack,
 
contacting
 
major
 
depositors
 
during
 
a
 
liquidity
 
concern).

■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Assign
 
IRTs
 
for
 
each
 
crisis
 
type
 
(ﬁ nancial,
 
operational,
 
reputational)
 
and
 
conduct
 
regular
 
simulation
 
drills.
 
M easure
 
response
 
times
 
and
 
identify
 
process
 
bottlenecks
 
for
 
improvement.
○
 
Cross-Functional
 
Coordination
■
 
Goal
:
 
Unify
 
efforts
 
among
 
ﬁnance,
 
operations,
 
IT,
 
communications,
 
and
 
member
 
relations
 
teams
 
for
 
swift,
 
coordinated
 
action.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Create
 
a
 
crisis
 
communication
 
channel
 
(e.g.,
 
a
 
secure
 
messaging
 
group)
 
to
 
provide
 
real-time
 
updates
 
to
 
key
 
stakeholders.
 
Conduct
 
mock
 
cross-department
 
scenarios
 
at
 
least
 
annually.
●
 
Contingency
 
Plans
 
for
 
High-Risk
 
Scenarios
 
○
 
Emergency
 
Liquidity
 
Injection
■
 
Approach
:
 
Secure
 
alternative
 
funding
 
sources
 
(e.g.,
 
interbank
 
lines
 
of
 
credit,
 
central
 
bank
 
facilities)
 
if
 
deposits
 
rapidly
 
decline
 
or
 
credit
 
availability
 
tightens.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Pre-negotiate
 
standby
 
credit
 
lines
 
and
 
maintain
 
updated
 
legal
 
documents.
 
Periodically
 
test
 
these
 
lines
 
to
 
conﬁrm
 
operational
 
readiness.
○
 
Business
 
Continuity
 
Plans
 
(BCPs)
■
 
Objective
:
 
Ensure
 
core
 
operations
 
(e.g.,
 
online
 
banking,
 
call
 
centers)
 
remain
 
functional
 
despite
 
system
 
failures
 
or
 
facility
 
closures.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Conduct
 
BCP
 
drills
 
every
 
six
 
months
 
to
 
conﬁrm
 
backup
 
site
 
readiness,
 
data
 
recovery
 
protocols,
 
and
 
staff
 
role
 
assignments.
Communication
 
Strategy
●
 
Internal
 
and
 
External
 
Protocols
 
○
 
Purpose
:
 
M aintain
 
member
 
trust
 
and
 
organizational
 
coherence
 
by
 
delivering
 
accurate,
 
timely
 
updates.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Draft
 
crisis-speciﬁc
 
communication
 
playbooks
 
detailing
 
which
 
individuals
 
or
 
teams
 
(Board
 
members,
 
executives)
 
must
 
be
 
notiﬁed
 
ﬁrst.
 
Include
 
a
 
timeline
 
for
 
updates
 
(e.g.,
 
initial
 
announcement
 
within
 
one
 
hour,
 
subsequent
 
updates
 
every
 
two
 
hours).
●
 
Pre-Approved
 
Templates
 
○
 
Consistency
 
and
 
Clarity
:
 
Prepare
 
press
 
releases,
 
member
 
emails,
 
and
 
social
 
media
 
statements
 
in
 
advance,
 
tailored
 
to
 
common
 
crisis
 
types
 
(e.g.,
 
data
 
breach,
 
service
 
disruption).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Keep
 
templates
 
concise
 
and
 
empathetic,
 
highlighting
 
immediate
 
actions
 
taken
 
and
 
advising
 
members
 
or
 
partners
 
on
 
steps
 
they
 
may
 
need
 
to
 
follow
 
(e.g.,
 
changing
 
passwords,
 
monitoring
 
accounts).

Post-Crisis
 
Analysis
●
 
Detailed
 
Review
 
of
 
Root
 
Causes
 
○
 
Objective
:
 
Identify
 
exactly
 
how
 
and
 
why
 
the
 
crisis
 
emerged,
 
including
 
any
 
systemic
 
gaps
 
in
 
policies,
 
training,
 
or
 
infrastructure.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Host
 
a
 
“lessons
 
learned”
 
workshop
 
within
 
30
 
days
 
of
 
crisis
 
resolution,
 
inviting
 
all
 
relevant
 
stakeholders.
 
Document
 
key
 
takeaways
 
and
 
assign
 
owners
 
for
 
follow-up
 
improvements.
●
 
Implementation
 
of
 
Process
 
Improvements
 
○
 
Prevention
 
of
 
Recurrence
:
 
Adjust
 
governance
 
structures,
 
risk
 
policies,
 
or
 
technical
 
safeguards
 
to
 
address
 
identiﬁed
 
vulnerabilities.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Develop
 
a
 
formalized
 
action
 
list
 
with
 
clear
 
deadlines
 
and
 
responsibilities
 
(e.g.,
 
“Complete
 
vulnerability
 
scans
 
monthly,”
 
“Update
 
credit
 
approval
 
thresholds
 
for
 
high-risk
 
sectors”).
 
Present
 
updates
 
to
 
the
 
Board
 
and
 
relevant
 
committees
 
until
 
all
 
tasks
 
are
 
closed.
Key
 
Metrics
 
for
 
Crisis
 
Management
1.
 
Time
 
to
 
Resolution
 
○
 
Deﬁnition
:
 
The
 
duration
 
from
 
the
 
moment
 
a
 
crisis
 
is
 
declared
 
to
 
its
 
containment
 
or
 
resolution.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Set
 
target
 
resolution
 
times
 
(e.g.,
 
24
 
hours
 
for
 
minor
 
IT
 
outages)
 
and
 
track
 
actual
 
performance.
 
If
 
repeated
 
lags
 
occur,
 
reevaluate
 
escalation
 
and
 
resource
 
allocation
 
protocols.
2.
 
Financial
 
Impact
 
Relative
 
to
 
Capital
 
Reserves
 
○
 
Purpose
:
 
Assess
 
the
 
monetary
 
damage
 
of
 
a
 
crisis
 
(losses,
 
ﬁnes,
 
missed
 
revenue)
 
compared
 
to
 
Desjardins’
 
capital
 
position.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
If
 
crisis-related
 
costs
 
exceed
 
a
 
predeﬁned
 
threshold
 
(e.g.,
 
5%
 
of
 
capital
 
reserves),
 
conduct
 
an
 
extraordinary
 
audit
 
to
 
explore
 
additional
 
resilience
 
measures—such
 
as
 
higher
 
reserve
 
targets
 
or
 
expanded
 
insurance
 
coverage.
By
 
implementing
 
a
 
robust
 
crisis
 
management
 
framework—covering
 
identiﬁcation,
 
response,
 
communication,
 
and
 
analysis—Desjardins
 
can
 
protect
 
member
 
conﬁdence
 
and
 
institutional
 
viability
 

under
 
extreme
 
stress.
 
Bank
 
directors
 
should
 
routinely
 
evaluate
 
and
 
reﬁne
 
these
 
procedures,
 
ensuring
 
that
 
the
 
organization
 
remains
 
prepared
 
for
 
evolving
 
threats
 
while
 
upholding
 
cooperative
 
principles
 
and
 
trust.

4.
 
M ember
 
Engagement
 
as

This

for

to

4.1
 
M ember-Centric

:

ﬁnancing,

ﬁnancial

:

:

Constantly

ﬁnancial

1.

○

:

emerging
 
ﬁnancial
 
behaviors
 
(e.g.,
 
increased
 
use
 
of
 
mobile
 
payments
 
or
 
niche
 
investment
 
products).
○
 
Feedback-Driven
 
Intelligence
:
 
Collect
 
both
 
qualitative
 
(surveys,
 
focus
 
groups)
 
and
 
quantitative
 
(usage
 
metrics,
 
NPS
 
scores)
 
data
 
to
 
form

of
 
member
 
needs.
○
 
Behavioral
 
Insights
:
 
Track
 
in-app
 
navigation
 
patterns
 
or
 
feature
 
click-through
 
rates
 
to
 
highlight
 
pain
 
points
 
or
 
particularly
 
popular
 
functionalities.
○
 
Actionable

:

these
 
data

into

uniﬁed
 
analytics

for

to

trends
 
(e.g.,

in
 
loan
 
requests
 
before

and
 
swiftly

offerings.
2.
 
Predictive
 
Analytics
 
for
 
Anticipation
 
○
 
Purpose
:
 
Use
 
machine
 
learning
 
models
 
to

member
 
behaviors
 
(e.g.,

of

○

:
 
Feed
 
external
 
factors
 
(m acro
 
trends,

algorithms.
 
For

or
 
reﬁnance
 
requests.

“M ember-Driven

4.2
 
Strengthening
 
Democratic
 
Processes
4.2.1
 
Advanced
 
Systems
 
for
 
M ember
 
Participation
A
 
thriving
 
cooperative
 
depends
 
on
 
active,
 
diverse
 
member
 
participation.
 
To
 
strengthen
 
democratic
 
processes
 
and
 
ensure
 
broad-based
 
engagement,
 
Desjardins
 
must
 
harness
 
digital
 
innovations
 
and
 
inclusive
 
meeting
 
formats.
 
Below
 
are
 
the
 
key
 
strategies
 
and
 
actionable
 
steps
 
for
 
directors
 
to
 
consider:
Digital
 
Voting
 
and
 
Participation
 
Platforms
1.
 
Secure,
 
Accessible
 
Systems
 
○
 
Blockchain-Based
 
Solutions
:
 
Employ
 
blockchain
 
or
 
other
 
decentralized
 
technologies
 
to
 
guarantee
 
tamper-proof
 
voting.
 
This
 
ensures
 
that
 
each
 
vote
 
is
 
unique,
 
transparent,
 
and
 
veriﬁable
 
without
 
compromising
 
member
 
privacy.
○
 
Mobile-Optimized
 
Interfaces
:
 
Provide
 
user-friendly
 
mobile
 
apps
 
or
 
websites
 
that
 
allow
 
members
 
to
 
vote
 
and
 
comment
 
on
 
proposals
 
remotely,
 
eliminating
 
the
 
need
 
for
 
travel
 
or
 
paper-based
 
ballots.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Run
 
pilot
 
programs
 
before
 
widespread
 
implementation.
 
Gather
 
feedback
 
on
 
system
 
usability
 
and
 
security
 
features.
 
Address
 
concerns
 
about
 
data
 
privacy,
 
and
 
provide
 
“how-to”
 
tutorials
 
for
 
less
 
tech-savvy
 
members.
2.
 
Multilingual
 
and
 
Inclusive
 
Access
 
○
 
Goal
:
 
Ensure
 
that
 
language
 
barriers
 
or
 
physical
 
limitations
 
do
 
not
 
exclude
 
any
 
member
 
from
 
exercising
 
their
 
voting
 
rights.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Offer
 
the
 
voting
 
platform
 
in
 
multiple
 
languages
 
commonly
 
used
 
among
 
Desjardins’
 
membership.
 
Incorporate
 
accessibility
 
features
 
(e.g.,
 
screen
 
readers,
 
large
 
text
 
options,
 
audio
 
prompts)
 
to
 
support
 
members
 
with
 
visual
 
or
 
auditory
 
challenges.
Real-Time
 
Participation
 
Analytics
1.
 
Dashboards
 
for

○
 
Purpose
:
 
Provide
 
an
 
at-a-glance

of

breakdowns,
 
and

rates.
○
 
Actionable

:

cycle.

2.
 
Identifying
 
Underrepresented
 
Groups
 
○
 
Process
:
 
M onitor
 
participation
 
data
 
to

are
 
not
 
engaging—whether
 
by

○

for

or

○

:

and

their

Inclusive

not

By

Desjardins

of

to
 
shaping

future.

to

yearly

in
 
the
 
annual
 
report.
3.
 
Satisfaction
 
Scores
 
Related
 
to
 
Democratic
 
Processes
 
○
 
Approach
:
 
Conduct
 
periodic
 
surveys
 
assessing
 
how
 
members
 
perceive
 
the
 
fairness,
 
transparency,
 
and
 
effectiveness
 
of
 
governance
 
activities.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Ask
 
speciﬁc
 
questions
 
about
 
recent
 
elections
 
or
 
strategic
 
votes
 
(e.g.,
 
“Did
 
you
 
feel
 
adequately
 
informed
 
about
 
the
 
issues
 
before
 
voting?”).
 
Use
 
feedback
 
to
 
reﬁne
 
communication
 
strategies
 
and
 
voting
 
platform
 
features.
By
 
systematically
 
educating
 
members
 
on
 
cooperative
 
principles,
 
rewarding
 
those
 
who
 
step
 
up
 
to
 
engage,
 
and
 
measuring
 
progress
 
against
 
clear
 
participation
 
and
 
diversity
 
metrics,
 
Desjardins
 
ensures
 
a
 
governance
 
culture
 
that
 
is
 
both
 
robust
 
and
 
inclusive.
 
This
 
holistic
 
approach
 
deepens
 
member
 
loyalty,
 
strengthens
 
leadership
 
pipelines,
 
and
 
upholds
 
the
 
foundational
 
values
 
that
 
have
 
made
 
Desjardins
 
a
 
leader
 
in
 
cooperative
 
banking.

By

Desjardins

Leadership
 
Identiﬁcation
 
Framework
1.
 
Deﬁning
 
Criteria
 
for
 
Potential

○

Principles
:

in

and

○
 
Performance
 
Track
 
Record
:

achievements
 
in

roles—such
 
as
 
exceeding
 
operational
 
targets,
 
successfully
 
implementing
 
member-focused
 
initiatives,
 
or
 
leading

○
 
Soft

and

:

(e.g.,

adaptability
 
to

(e.g.,

strategies),
 
and

to
 
drive
 
innovation.
○

:

that

(project

and

(p eer
 
reviews,
 
innovation
 
awards).

:

:

:

plans

By

can

and

in

ﬁnancial

5.1.2
 
Rotational
 
Leadership
 
Strategies
 
for
 
Cross-Functional
 
Expertise
Rotational
 
leadership
 
programs
 
help
 
Desjardins
 
develop
 
agile,
 
well-rounded
 
leaders
 
who
 
can
 
effectively
 
collaborate
 
across
 
diverse
 
operational,
 
strategic,
 
and
 
community-driven
 
contexts.
 
By
 
creating
 
structured
 
rotations,
 
supporting
 
participants
 
with
 
mentorship,
 
and
 
rigorously
 
measuring
 
outcomes,
 
Desjardins
 
ensures
 
its
 
leadership
 
pipeline
 
remains
 
strong,
 
innovative,
 
and
 
aligned
 
with
 
cooperative
 
values.
Purpose
 
of
 
Rotation
 
Programs
●
 
Develop
 
Organization-Wide
 
Perspective
 
○
 
Goal
:
 
Equip
 
upcoming
 
leaders
 
with
 
a
 
holistic
 
understanding
 
of
 
Desjardins’
 
functions—from
 
front-line
 
services
 
in
 
retail
 
banking
 
to
 
the
 
complexities
 
of
 
risk
 
management
 
and
 
technology
 
innovation.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Require
 
participants
 
to
 
document
 
key
 
lessons
 
and
 
operational
 
insights
 
after
 
each
 
rotation.
 
Encourage
 
them
 
to
 
share
 
these
 
takeaways
 
with
 
peers
 
via
 
brown-bag
 
sessions
 
or
 
internal
 
forums.
●
 
Break
 
Down
 
Departmental
 
Silos
 
○
 
Approach
:
 
Rotate
 
candidates
 
through
 
multiple
 
departments,
 
such
 
as
 
retail
 
banking,
 
risk
 
management,
 
technology
 
and
 
innovation,
 
and
 
community
 
engagement.
 
This
 
cross-exposure
 
fosters
 
a
 
mindset
 
of
 
collaboration
 
and
 
member-centric
 
problem-solving.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Incorporate
 
project-based
 
assignments
 
during
 
each
 
rotation.
 
For
 
example,
 
a
 
rotation
 
in
 
community
 
engagement
 
might
 
include
 
organizing
 
a
 
ﬁnancial
 
literacy
 
workshop,
 
while
 
a
 
stint
 
in
 
technology
 
could
 
involve
 
piloting
 
a
 
new
 
mobile
 
banking
 
feature.
Designing
 
Rotational
 
Programs
●
 
Structure
 
and
 
Duration
 
○
 
Timeframe
:
 
Plan
 
rotations
 
lasting
 
18–36
 
months,
 
with
 
each
 
segment
 
spanning
 
3–9
 
months,
 
depending
 
on
 
the
 
complexity
 
of
 
the
 
function.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Kick
 
off
 
each
 
rotation
 
with
 
a
 
structured
 
orientation,
 
clarifying
 
departmental
 
goals,
 
performance
 
metrics,
 
and
 
the
 
rotation
 
participant’s
 
speciﬁc
 
project
 
or
 
responsibility.
●
 
International
 
or
 
Inter-Cooperative
 
Placements
 

○
 
Diverse
 
Insights
:
 
Consider
 
sending
 
select
 
leaders
 
to
 
partner
 
cooperatives
 
or
 
international
 
branches
 
to
 
gain
 
exposure
 
to
 
different
 
regulatory
 
environments,
 
cultural
 
contexts,
 
and
 
innovative
 
practices.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Formalize
 
exchange
 
agreements
 
with

cooperative
 
networks
 
to
 
streamline
 
the
 
placement
 
process.
 
Ensure
 
participants
 
have
 
clear
 
learning
 
objectives
 
and
 
post-rotation
 
debrief
 
sessions
 
for
 
knowledge
 
transfer.
Mentorship
 
and
 
Support
●
 
Pairing
 
Participants
 
with

Mentors
 
○
 
Guidance
:
 
Assign
 
an

or

to

and

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:

between

and

to

progress
 
on

and

●

Coaching
 
○
 
Integration
 
of
 
Lessons
:
 
Provide

coaching
 
sessions
 
or

that

learned
 
across

area.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Encourage
 
participants
 
to
 
maintain
 
a
 
“learning
 
journal,”
 
recording
 
insights
 
and
 
reﬂecting
 
on
 
how
 
best
 
to
 
apply

in

Share
 
highlights
 
in

sessions
 
to

peer-to-peer
 
learning.
Outcomes
 
and
 
Measurement
●

Improvements
 
in
 
Subsequent
 
Roles
 
○
 
Assessment
:

Look

(e.g.,

●

and

Rates
 
○
 
Goal
:

at

:

●
 
Organizational
 
Beneﬁts
 
○

:

alumni

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:

By

Over

5.2
 
Culture
 
of
 
Excellence
5.2.1
 
Embedding
 
Accountability
 
and
 
Innovation
 
into
 
Leadership
 
Practices
A
 
strong
 
culture
 
of
 
excellence
 
at
 
Desjardins
 
stems
 
from
 
leaders
 
who
 
are
 
both
 
accountable
 
and
 
innovative.
 
To
 
maintain
 
a
 
high-performance
 
environment
 
that
 
aligns
 
with
 
cooperative
 
values,
 
bank
 
directors
 
must
 
ensure
 
leaders
 
have
 
clear
 
metrics,
 
structured
 
review
 
processes,
 
and
 
the
 
freedom
 
to
 
experiment
 
with
 
new
 
ideas.
 
Below
 
are
 
key
 
steps
 
and
 
actionable
 
strategies
 
to
 
achieve
 
this.
Deﬁning
 
Accountability
 
Metrics
1.
 
Alignment
 
with
 
Cooperative
 
Values
 
○
 
Approach
:
 
Tie
 
leadership
 
performance
 
directly
 
to
 
Desjardins’
 
mission—focusing
 
on
 
member
 
satisfaction,
 
community
 
impact,
 
and
 
social
 
responsibility
 
in
 
addition
 
to
 
ﬁnancial
 
outcomes.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Break
 
down
 
each
 
metric
 
into
 
quantiﬁable
 
targets.
 
For
 
example,
 
set
 
a
 
minimum
 
increase
 
in
 
member
 
satisfaction
 
scores
 
(e.g.,
 
5%
 
year-over-year)
 
and
 
track
 
progress
 
quarterly.
 
Include
 
environmental,
 
social,
 
and
 
governance
 
(ESG)
 
goals—such
 
as
 
reducing
 
operational
 
carbon
 
footprint
 
or
 
increasing
 
the
 
percentage
 
of
 
loans
 
dedicated
 
to
 
green
 
projects.
2.
 
Performance
 
Dashboards
 
○
 
Purpose
:
 
Provide
 
leaders
 
with
 
a
 
real-time
 
snapshot
 
of
 
how
 
they’re
 
meeting
 
member
 
engagement,
 
innovation,
 
and
 
operational
 
targets.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Automate
 
dashboard
 
updates
 
using
 
data
 
from
 
relevant
 
internal
 
systems
 
(e.g.,
 
CRM
 
for
 
member
 
satisfaction,
 
project
 
management
 
tools
 
for
 
innovation
 
initiatives).
 
Require
 
monthly
 
or
 
quarterly
 
reviews
 
at
 
the
 
leadership
 
level
 
to
 
identify
 
variances
 
and
 
plan
 
corrective
 
measures.
Accountability
 
Structures
1.
 
Structured
 
Review
 
Processes
 
○

Reviews
:

consistent

(e.g.,

or

and
 
team
 
leaders
 
to

goal

and

○

:
 
Encourage

to

and

accountability.

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:

“review

and

action
 
items.
 
Distribute

to

or

to

and
 
follow-through.
2.
 
Performance
 
Management
 
Software
 
○
 
Usage
:

that

metrics,
 
and

in

○

Tip
:

(e.g.,

so

Fostering
 
Innovation

Safe
 
Spaces

○

or

Forces
:

ideas,
 
or

improvements.
 
Provide
 
a

and

to

and

quickly.
○
 
Rewarding
 
Risk-Taking
:
 
Acknowledge

who

new
 
concepts—even
 
if

ﬁnal

or

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:

“lessons

debrief

project
 
to

insights
 
across

2.
 
Open
 
Dialogue
 
on
 
Future
 
Trends
 
○
 
Biannual

Summits
:
 
Invite
 
leaders
 
to

new
 
ideas,

changes,
 
and

solutions
 
to
 
emerging
 
challenges
 
(e.g.,
 
ﬁntech
 
competition,

risk).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Collect
 
actionable
 
ideas
 
during

and

a

roadmap.
 
Assign
 
executive
 
sponsors
 
to

milestones,
 
ensuring
 
continuous
 
progress.
By
 
clearly

metrics,
 
implementing
 
rigorous

processes,
 
and

atmosphere
 
that
 
rewards

and

Desjardins
 
reinforces

of

For

and

ahead

on

innovation.



5.2.2
 
Aligning
 
Incentives
 
with

Mission
To

a
 
culture
 
of
 
excellence,
 
Desjardins
 
must

that

and

outcomes.
 
By

to

and

aligned

principles,
 
the
 
organization
 
fosters
 
leadership
 
behaviors
 
that
 
prioritize

over

gains.
Monetary
 
and
 
Non-Monetary
 
Incentives
1.
 
Mission-Aligned
 
Performance
 
Bonuses
 
○
 
Approach
:
 
M ove
 
beyond
 
pure
 
proﬁt-driven
 
rewards
 
by
 
tying
 
variable

to
 
metrics
 
such
 
as

equity
 
growth,
 
sustainability
 
benchmarks
 
(e.g.,

in

or

and

scores.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
For
 
each
 
leadership
 
role,
 
designate
 
a
 
set
 
percentage
 
of
 
the
 
annual

linked
 
to
 
cooperative
 
outcomes.

reinvestment
 
targets,

in

6.1.1
 
Evaluating
 
and

Careful

and

of
 
ﬁntech

can

This

and

that

processes
 
and
 
support

Assessment
 
of
 
Fintech
 
Opportunities
1.
 
Identify
 
Critical
 
Operational
 
Areas
 
○

Areas
:

departments
 
or
 
workﬂows

and

■

:

to

:

(K YC)

that

and

compliance.
■
 
Loan

and
 
Credit
 
Scoring
:
 
Use
 
AI-driven
 
solutions
 
to
 
accelerate
 
decision-making
 
and
 
reduce
 
defaults
 
through
 
better
 
credit
 
risk
 
assessments.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:

an
 
internal

to

and

bottlenecks.
 
Invite
 
frontline
 
employees
 
(e.g.,

to

ideas

pain

○

Implementation
 
Roadmap
1.
 
Pilot
 
Programs
 
○
 
Controlled
 
Environments
:
 
Launch
 
new
 
ﬁntech
 
solutions
 
in
 
a
 
limited
 
scope—perhaps

or

member
 
segment—to
 
collect

and
 
user

○

:

success

for

(e.g.,
 
loan
 
application
 
turnaround

user
 
satisfaction
 
scores).
 
If

conduct
 
root
 
cause

before

deployment.
2.
 
Feedback
 
Mechanisms
 
○

Improvement
:

and

through

or

and

and

:

for

as

evolves.

:

:

ﬂagged

Tools

Ethical

Technology

Performance
 
Metrics
1.
 
Decision-Making
 
Speed
 
and
 
Accuracy
 
○
 
Measurement
:
 
Track
 
how
 
quickly
 
loan
 
decisions,
 
fraud
 
alerts,
 
or

service
 
issues
 
are
 
resolved
 
post-AI/analytics
 
implementation.
 
Compare
 
with
 
baseline
 
numbers.

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
If
 
results
 
plateau
 
or
 
decline,
 
investigate
 
whether
 
staff
 
need
 
additional
 
training
 
or
 
if

need
 
recalibration.
2.
 
Fraud
 
Prevention
 
Rates
 
○
 
Goal
:
 
Reduce
 
fraud-related
 
losses
 
by
 
a
 
set
 
percentage
 
(e.g.,
 
20%)
 
within
 
a
 
year
 
of

AI-based
 
detection
 
systems.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Track
 
false
 
positives
 
(legitimate
 
transactions
 
ﬂagged
 
as
 
fraud)
 
and
 
false
 
negatives
 
(fraud
 
that
 
slips
 
through)
 
to
 
improve
 
model
 
precision
 
and
 
maintain
 
member
 
trust.

Satisfaction
 
via

○

(N PS),

and

tied
 
to

offers
 
or

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Incorporate
 
feedback
 
mechanisms
 
(e.g.,
 
a
 
quick
 
survey
 
after
 
an
 
AI-driven
 
recommendation)
 
to
 
collect
 
real-time
 
member
 
sentiment
 
and
 
reﬁne
 
personalization
 
strategies.
By
 
thoughtfully
 
implementing
 
AI
 
and
 
data
 
analytics,
 
Desjardins
 
can
 
streamline
 
internal
 
operations,
 
mitigate
 
risk,
 
and

increasingly

to

while

Structured

clear

indicators,
 
and
 
an

to
 
ethical
 
practices
 
ensure
 
these
 
technologies
 
enhance,
 
rather

Desjardins’
 
member-ﬁrst
 
mission.

banking.

7.

This

It

that
 
enhance

The

to
 
position
 
Desjardins
 
as
 
a
 
leader
 
in
 
sustainable
 
cooperative
 
banking.

Internal

for
 
Operations

Footprint
 
○

Transition
:

or

(R OI).

:

○

Use
:

for

○
 
Green
 
Loan
 
Portfolios
:
 
Allocate
 
a
 
deﬁned
 
percentage
 
of
 
the
 
overall
 
loan
 
book
 
to
 
projects
 
that
 
signiﬁcantly
 
reduce
 
carbon
 
emissions
 
(e.g.,

installations,

transportation).

Tip
:

(e.g.,
 
+5%

each

and

to

ensuring

at

levels.
○

:

:

with

emissions.

○

7.2

and

8.1

8.1.1

aligned

These

Below

Building

Partnerships
1.

Complementary
 
Institutions
 
○
 
Approach
:

:

track

Prioritize

regions
 
or

ﬁnance
 
expertise.

○

:

:

ﬁnancial

(e.g.,

:

to

○

Tip
:

Real-Time
 
Risk
 
Monitoring

1.

Tracking
 
○
 
Approach
:

uniﬁed

that

caisses,

to

○

:

to

daily.

(e.g.,

failures).

○

:

to

or
 
operational
 
workﬂows.
○

:

of

on

and

detection

as

:

Risk

1.

Potential

○

:

(e.g.,

“At
 
a
 
Glance”)
 
for
 
busy
 
readers.
Ethical
 
Business
 
Practices
1.
 
Embedding
 
Cooperative
 
Principles
 
in
 
Decision-Making
 
○
 
Member-Centric
 
Approach
:
 
Always
 
evaluate
 
whether
 
business
 
ventures,
 
product
 
launches,
 
or
 
policy
 
changes
 
align
 
with
 
Desjardins’
 
foundational
 
goal:
 
serving
 
members
 
over
 
pure
 
proﬁt
 
pursuits.
○
 
Avoiding
 
Poor
 
ESG
 
Partnerships
:
 
Vet
 
potential
 
partners
 
or
 
investment
 
opportunities
 
for
 
environmental
 
and
 
social
 
performance.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
M aintain
 
a
 
public
 
“Ethical
 
Exclusion
 
List”
 
outlining
 
industries
 
or
 
practices
 
(e.g.,
 
fossil
 
fuel
 
ventures,
 
exploitative
 
labor)
 
that
 
Desjardins
 
will
 
not
 
support,
 
underscoring
 
the
 
organization’s
 
standards.

2.
 
Ethics
 
Committee
 
Oversight
 
○
 
High-Impact
 
Decision
 
Review
:
 
Task
 
the
 
committee
 
with
 
assessing
 
major
 
initiatives—such
 
as
 
mergers,
 
large-scale
 
partnerships,
 
or
 
controversial
 
product
 
launches—for
 
alignment
 
with
 
Desjardins’
 
cooperative
 
mission.
○
 
Conﬂict
 
Resolution
:
 
Provide
 
a
 
clear,
 
conﬁdential
 
forum
 
where
 
employees,
 
leadership,
 
or
 
Board
 
members
 
can
 
refer
 
ethical
 
dilemmas.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Publish
 
a
 
quarterly
 
“Ethics
 
Digest”
 
summarizing
 
major
 
ethical
 
decisions
 
(in
 
an
 
anonymized
 
form)
 
to
 
showcase
 
transparency
 
and
 
maintain
 
accountability.
Whistleblower
 
Programs
1.
 
Anonymous
 
Reporting
 
Channels
 
○
 
Conﬁdentiality
 
and
 
Protection
:
 
Guarantee
 
that
 
whistleblowers
 
face
 
no
 
retaliation
 
and
 
that
 
their
 
identities
 
remain
 
protected.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Offer
 
multiple
 
reporting
 
options—like
 
hotlines,
 
web
 
portals,
 
or
 
secure
 
messaging—to
 
accommodate
 
differing
 
comfort
 
levels
 
and
 
technology
 
access
 
among
 
employees.
2.
 
Transparent
 
Investigation
 
Process
 
○
 
Procedure
:
 
Outline
 
clear
 
steps
 
for
 
receiving,
 
investigating,
 
and
 
resolving
 
whistleblower
 
claims.
 
Communicate
 
expected
 
timelines
 
for
 
each
 
stage.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Regularly
 
publish
 
aggregate
 
statistics
 
on
 
cases
 
(e.g.,
 
the
 
number
 
of
 
reports
 
ﬁled,
 
categories
 
of
 
issues,
 
general
 
outcomes)
 
in
 
a
 
dedicated
 
whistleblower
 
section
 
of
 
the
 
annual
 
report.
 
Emphasize
 
improvements
 
made
 
based
 
on
 
these
 
ﬁndings.

:

high

Metrics

Scores

:

or

(N PS)

(e.g.,

Whistleblower

Resolutions
 
○
 
Measurement
:

the

to

and

(e.g.,

Actionable

:

in

to

needing

or

as

in

or

Ethical
 
Compliance
 
Rate

○
 
Approach
:

and

audits,

to

and

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:

“compliance

By

in

also

and

of

who
 
depend
 
on
 
Desjardins’
 
principled
 
approach
 
to
 
ﬁnancial
 
services.

9.2.2
 
Periodic
 
Audits
 
to
 
Ensure
 
Adherence
 
to
 
Cooperative
 
Principles
Consistent
 
and
 
well-structured
 
audits
 
are
 
essential
 
for
 
verifying
 
that
 
Desjardins
 
remains
 
faithful
 
to
 
its
 
cooperative
 
values
 
while
 
meeting
 
operational,
 
regulatory,
 
and
 
ethical
 
standards.
 
These
 
audits,
 
both
 
internal
 
and
 
external,
 
help
 
identify
 
areas
 
of
 
improvement,
 
maintain
 
transparency,
 
and
 
foster
 
continuous
 
alignment
 
with
 
Desjardins’
 
mission
 
of
 
serving
 
members
 
and
 
communities.
Internal
 
Audit
 
Processes
1.
 
Regular
 
Audits
 
for
 
Cooperative
 
Alignment
 
○
 
Scope
:
■
 
Financial
 
Audits
:
 
Review
 
allocations
 
of
 
funds
 
and
 
resources
 
to
 
conﬁrm
 
that
 
expenditures
 
support
 
cooperative
 
objectives
 
(e.g.,
 
community
 
investments,
 
affordable
 
ﬁnancial
 
products).
■
 
Governance
 
Audits
:
 
Evaluate
 
how
 
inclusively
 
decisions
 
are
 
made—ensuring
 
member
 
participation,
 
transparency,
 
and
 
equitable
 
representation.
■
 
Sustainability
 
Audits
:
 
Assess
 
ESG
 
(E nvironmental,
 
Social,
 
and
 
Governance)
 
progress,
 
verifying
 
that
 
green
 
initiatives
 
and
 
socially
 
responsible
 
commitments
 
are
 
on
 
track.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Implement
 
a
 
rotating
 
audit
 
schedule
 
(e.g.,
 
monthly,
 
quarterly)
 
focusing
 
on
 
speciﬁc
 
departments
 
or
 
functions.
 
Use
 
targeted
 
sampling
 
in
 
high-risk
 
areas—such
 
as
 
large-scale
 
loan
 
approvals
 
or
 
new
 
product
 
launches—to
 
detect
 
issues
 
early.
2.
 
Risk-Based
 
Auditing
 
Techniques
 
○
 
Focus
 
on
 
High-Risk
 
Domains
:
 
Concentrate
 
audit
 
efforts
 
where
 
the
 
stakes
 
or
 
complexities
 
are
 
highest
 
(e.g.,
 
major
 
capital
 
projects,
 
partnerships
 
with
 
external
 
vendors,
 
digital
 
transformation
 
initiatives).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
M aintain
 
a
 
“Risk
 
Heat
 
M ap”
 
and
 
update
 
it
 
after
 
each
 
audit
 
cycle.
 
If
 
certain
 
areas
 
repeatedly
 
show
 
vulnerabilities—like
 
compliance
 
gaps
 
in
 
a
 
speciﬁc
 
region—allocate
 
additional
 
auditing
 
resources
 
and
 
training
 
for
 
that
 
region.
External
 
Audit
 
Engagements

Independent
 
Validation
 
○
 
Purpose
:

(e.g.,
 
specialized
 
cooperative

auditors)
 
to
 
assess
 
compliance
 
with
 
national
 
and

and
 
alignment
 
with

benchmarks.

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Include
 
a
 
cooperative
 
ethos
 
module
 
in

scope.
 
Ask

to
 
evaluate
 
how
 
well
 
Desjardins
 
adheres
 
to
 
principles
 
of

and

beyond
 
conventional
 
ﬁnancial

Transparent
 
Reporting
 
to

:

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:

audit
 
highlights
 
(e.g.,

for

recommended
 
actions)
 
in

language.
 
Encourage

or

to
 
maintain
 
dialogue
 
and
 
trust.
Audit
 
Action
 
Plans
1.
 
Developing
 
Follow-Up
 
Measures
 
○
 
Timelines
 
and
 
Accountability
:
 
Translate
 
each
 
audit
 
recommendation
 
into
 
a
 
clear
 
set
 
of
 
steps
 
with
 
assigned
 
owners
 
(e.g.,
 
departmental
 
heads)
 
and
 
realistic
 
deadlines.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Use
 
project
 
management
 
software
 
to
 
track
 
progress
 
on
 
recommended
 
changes
 
(e.g.,
 
policy
 
updates,
 
training
 
programs).
 
Provide
 
monthly
 
or
 
quarterly
 
status
 
updates
 
to
 
the
 
Board
 
and
 
relevant
 
committees.
2.
 
Reﬁning
 
Policies
 
and
 
Risk
 
Management
 
○
 
Insight
 
Utilization
:
 
Leverage
 
audit
 
ﬁndings
 
to
 
update
 
internal
 
rules,
 
processes,
 
and
 
control
 
mechanisms—especially
 
in
 
response
 
to
 
recurring
 
issues
 
(e.g.,

overlooked

○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Hold
 
a

with

to

improvements.
 
Align
 
these
 
improvements
 
with
 
Desjardins’
 
strategic
 
objectives,
 
ensuring
 
that
 
each

change
 
reinforces
 
cooperative
 
values.
Metrics
 
for
 
Audit
 
Effectiveness
1.
 
Frequency
 
and
 
Severity
 
of
 
Findings
 
○
 
Measurement
:
 
Track
 
how
 
many
 
issues
 
each
 
audit
 
uncovers
 
and
 
categorize
 
them
 
by
 
severity
 
(e.g.,
 
minor,
 
moderate,
 
high-risk).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
If
 
major
 
ﬁndings
 
spike
 
in
 
a
 
particular
 
domain
 
(e.g.,
 
data
 
privacy),
 
form
 
a
 
specialized
 
task
 
force
 
to
 
address
 
these
 
issues
 
comprehensively
 
rather
 
than
 
piecemeal.

2.
 
Percentage
 
of
 
Resolved
 
Recommendations
 
○
 
Goal
:
 
Close
 
the
 
loop
 
on
 
audit
 
ﬁndings
 
within
 
deﬁned
 
timeframes
 
(e.g.,
 
resolve
 
90%
 
of
 
all
 
high-priority
 
recommendations
 
within
 
90
 
days).
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Use
 
dashboards
 
or
 
progress
 
trackers
 
that
 
highlight
 
overdue
 
tasks,
 
prompting
 
quick
 
follow-ups
 
from
 
responsible
 
managers
 
or
 
committees.
3.
 
Post-Audit
 
Improvements
 
in
 
Efficiency
 
and
 
Compliance
 
○
 
Assessment
:
 
Evaluate
 
whether
 
operational
 
workﬂows
 
become
 
more
 
efficient
 
or
 
compliance
 
rates
 
rise
 
after
 
implementing
 
audit
 
recommendations.
○
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Conduct
 
a
 
mini-audit
 
or
 
review
 
six
 
months
 
post-implementation
 
to
 
conﬁrm
 
that
 
recommended
 
changes
 
have
 
successfully
 
mitigated
 
the
 
identiﬁed
 
risks.
By
 
conducting
 
regular
 
internal
 
and
 
external
 
audits,
 
Desjardins
 
ensures
 
that
 
all

of
 
its
 
operations—from
 
ﬁnancial
 
management
 
to

practices—remain
 
in

with

Bank

in

acting
 
on
 
ﬁndings
 
promptly,
 
and

progress
 
transparently
 
to
 
reinforce
 
member
 
conﬁdence
 
and
 
uphold
 
Desjardins’
 
core
 
values.

10.
 
Performance
 
M anagement
 
and
 
KPIs
This
 
section
 
establishes
 
a
 
framework
 
for
 
deﬁning,
 
monitoring,
 
and
 
optimizing
 
performance
 
at
 
Desjardins.
 
It
 
integrates
 
ﬁnancial,
 
non-ﬁnancial,
 
and
 
strategic

into
 
actionable
 
insights,
 
ensuring
 
alignment
 
with
 
organizational
 
goals
 
and
 
cooperative
 
principles.
10.1
 
Deﬁning
 
Success
 
M etrics
A
 
robust
 
performance
 
management
 
framework
 
requires
 
looking
 
beyond
 
traditional
 
proﬁtability
 
measures
 
to
 
capture
 
Desjardins’
 
impact
 
on
 
members,
 
communities,
 
and
 
sustainability
 
objectives.
 
By
 
incorporating
 
both
 
ﬁnancial
 
and
 
non-ﬁnancial
 
KPIs,
 
Desjardins
 
ensures
 
that
 
growth
 
and
 
success
 
remain
 
ﬁrmly
 
anchored
 
in
 
cooperative
 
principles.
10.1.1
 
Expanding
 
Metrics
 
Beyond
 
Proﬁtability
1.
 
Member
 
Equity
 
and
 
Satisfaction
 
○
 
Year-Over-Year
 
Growth
 
in
 
Member
 
Equity
■
 
Purpose
:
 
Track
 
the
 
ﬁnancial
 
value
 
members
 
derive
 
through
 
dividends,
 
proﬁt-sharing,
 
or
 
returns
 
on
 
cooperative
 
investments.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Compare
 
quarterly
 
and
 
annual
 
results
 
across
 
different
 
member
 
segments
 
(e.g.,
 
long-standing
 
members
 
vs.
 
new
 
entrants)
 
to
 
see
 
which
 
groups
 
beneﬁt
 
most
 
and
 
where
 
further
 
support
 
might
 
be
 
needed.
○
 
Net
 
Promoter
 
Score
 
(NPS)
 
and
 
Complaint
 
Resolution
■
 
Goal
:
 
Gauge
 
member
 
loyalty
 
and
 
satisfaction
 
by
 
evaluating
 
how
 
likely
 
they
 
are
 
to
 
recommend
 
Desjardins
 
to
 
friends,
 
family,
 
or
 
peers,
 
alongside
 
how
 
effectively
 
Desjardins
 
resolves
 
complaints.
■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:
 
Set
 
a
 
target
 
NPS
 
improvement
 
rate
 
each
 
quarter
 
(e.g.,
 
+5
 
points).
 
W hen
 
complaints
 
spike
 
(e.g.,
 
after
 
new
 
product
 
launches),
 
set
 
up
 
cross-functional
 
“complaint
 
resolution
 
squads”
 
to
 
address
 
issues
 
quickly
 
and
 
reﬁne
 
processes.
2.
 
Reinvestment
 
Impact
 
○
 
Community-Focused
 
Investments
 
as

Percentage
 
of
 
Proﬁts
■
 
Objective
:
 
M easure
 
how
 
much
 
of
 
Desjardins’
 
earnings
 
ﬂow
 
back
 
into

Actionable

:

“Community

Scores”
 
detailing
 
how

investments
 
directly
 
beneﬁt
 
members—highlighting,

or

○
 
Outcomes
 
of
 
Reinvestments
■
 
Approach
:
 
Track
 
speciﬁc
 
metrics
 
such
 
as
 
jobs
 
created,
 
the

of

in

■
 
Actionable
 
Tip
:

with

NGOs
 
or

to

and

3.
 
ESG
 
Metrics
 
○
 
ESG-Compliant

(AUM)
■
 
Signiﬁcance
:

the

aligned

Actionable

:
 
Aim
 
for

○

Sustainability
■
 
Examples
:
 
Reductions
 
in
